et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and he leaves it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the heat.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter or bath as long as his body is a little warm, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will go away all and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery of such medicines, except after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Diachorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat hair, it helps a lot;
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and this cauterization must be done in such a way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take another, and oil it well, and put it on the crease that is between the thumb of the foot and the other which is called a flick.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After take dry goat hair, and hold it in fire until it becomes charcoal, and put it on the wool, and leave it until it is burned;
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and again try, and do not stop doing so as long as you think sensible that it comes up to the thigh, and that the pain is stopped;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this way of cauterizing is called "cauterize of goat".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain at the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or by sitting down or by pounding, or by too great an evacuation, or by the appearance of expanded cold material, no one of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except that which comes from the infusion of cold material.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is appropriate that after the patient has voided any foul pills or similar things, you do it on his back, where the pain persists, three lines signed with an inch, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and the quantity that the patient can bear;
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and be done cauterization according to the cauterize which is called "poins";
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see, do three cauterizations or four at the cauterize with a blade according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the sign of the beginning is that they have tight posture when they stand up, and fear;
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you will find in the back of the spine of the two and in us the appearance that comes on top of the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this person and you see him healed, if he is cauterized with the cauldron of fire according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	Let the fire cautery each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with a piercing cautery two or three lines, and let the burns be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After cure the area until it is healthy according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply cauterization to a ganglion that is in a nerve's spine.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints' pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When the joints hurt from moisture that spreads to each limb of the body, and when the pain comes in pieces, which the people properly call "gout," and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this way:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	make the fire cautery inside the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary for you to hold on the face of the foot, make a fire cautery with all the fire cautery that is called "no point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come only to the knees and to other joints, and it happens many times, make cauterization on each knee with three cauterizations or four of each part, all with olive oil cauterization;
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you have more work to do, if you make it more, but do not hold your hand firmly except when the spine of the knee is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains go down to the knees and back, administer the cautery that we have spoken about in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, then make a point to enter the fingers two lines.
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there remains any pain in both, then make a point on each joint and on the hair of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come just as the cuts or just as the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and give good government to the patient and apply remedies.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	Because if you do good management and you purify the pus, then you will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	about the surgery of the sick
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture occurs in the face, and the flesh falls down to the bones and is newly happened, so that when you cure him, he should not rub himself any more;
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and let him use things that cover his belly, so that the end may come off his belly;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after he has made himself sit on his back between your hands, and commands him to let his hair grow until the boil is healed, and brings it to your hands, and signs from one side of the wound on the bone with the fingernail, and all that looks like half a circle above the neck;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then heat up the cauldron of which this is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it seems solid.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then put the balls back in their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the assistant dyes his hand so that it does not turn back;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and operate well on the patient's legs, and put a cloth and an assistant on his legs, and another on his feet that will dye his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then place the cauldron on his signet ring on all your hand, and keep it in place until you reach the bone, and if you don't hit it the first time, try again a few more times until you do;
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and be careful that the flame does not escape when you operate with the cauldron;
que tu ne le brulasses;	so you don't burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and so that by chance the patient doesn't die, or any other harm is done.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you come only to the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cautters of children be subtle according to their measure, and of great people also great according to their measure;
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days cure leu the fire cautery so that the ostentation is cured;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after the cure other treatments as long as he is healthy, and lay the patient on his back for 40 days with the wound well soldered;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that its renewals be prolonged, so that the boil does not rise when he goes to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, a well-made bandage is given to him, and it is applied for another 40 days;
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and has good rest, that he works little and guards against too much drinking and eating, and against high-pitched yelling;
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he has taught this instruction, then he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in his chalk.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the uterine rupture
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When wounds come in other bellies and are connected, and you see that they no longer grow, then you make the fire cautery according to its quantity, and burn the third of it.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the above said that one should cauterize with the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first the sign the place of the navel and make a line through the largeness on the rupture, and another away from it, and all your hand in every cauterized claw.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizes are lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in no member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in no member, or from sitting or from hurting, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not useful, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with fire which is called "poins", and make the cauterize according to the length of the member and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of torments and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if he is healed with the first cautery, it is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	this name, begin another cautery on top of that one, for the custom is that it must grow in the member closest to him, so that you make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	from healing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The meseile are not aided at all by cautery, nor do the diseases arise from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy alone.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	If you see that the disease is at the beginning, and it is healed according to what we have said in the division, and does not stop or stay, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the whole disease, then you make five cauteries on top:
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I cut off the head at the neck, and the other goes to the front at the end of the hair.
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and I behind at the back on the nape/neck;
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and I leave it so that the fire cautery comes to the bone, and so that the wind/steam of the bad humors can come out,
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and I cauterize on the top according to what is in front of it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if it gets mixed everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it loses clearly, if you set the fire cautery that we have spoken at the head, and I cauterize on its neck, and II cauterizes on the spine of the back/neck, and VI cauterizes on the spine of the back/neck, and I great one on the top/skull, and another small one, and II on the shoulders;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and 2 on the knives, and 2 on the tendons of the foot, and 1 on each joint of the hand and the foot, and on the creases of the hands;
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and beware of the nerves that are above the knees when you stand, so as not to burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and do not make any fire cautery on the bone of the hand, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that the more fire cauteries I make, the more help I give, and the more benefit it brings;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the patient does not feel pain at the fire cautery as much as the healthy person feels it, because the body is already so corrupted;
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After care let him sit with flour of times with honey and other cures as long as he is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When the swelling comes on any member and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not yet healed, then you must make fire cauteries on the member according to its size and smallness;
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cauterization go a little way into the flesh of the back.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the doctor applies ointments as long as he is well.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And do not apply fire cauterization to the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that disposes the member, and thus if it is fractured;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and in no way does one interfere with them unless one knows the members and outlets of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease that is called "albarias" is awakened, and the medicine of it is useless, then let the cauterization be made with a small fire cautery, according to the quantity of flesh of the back, until the blotch is moved, and its color is changed;
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then the doctor applies flour of times and lentils with oil of roses and leaves of plantain, and blood of turtle and blood of almond, each a part;
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and make them all together, and bind them with a cloth, and keep them in place until they are well.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for syphilis by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the itch begins to appear, and you see it stopping, if you cauterize with a fire cautery that seems like a circle, all around the itch's circumference.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And moreover, the surgeon should tell you to make a fire cautery at the center of the ulcer;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and moreover, this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it come about;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and the most right thing is that it be cauterized from within, at the cautery that is called "circular", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When anyone has a disease that is called "adebelati", and it delays dying or because of the excess blood that it makes or because of the eagerness of the sick person when he is very old (that is to say, too much) and he has little blood, or because of the age;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see him hasten to die:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then cauterize it with small caustics while pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards leave it like this.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she is eager to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you pierce it throughout the whole cautery, let the cautery be very hot.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterization has penetrated the cure, and is such a cauterization that the patient feels the heat in some way that the course of the pus is controlled.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease that is called "corrodens", and is nothing other than a putrid mass of a member, because it corrodes the members as much as the fire dries up the wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see a disease in which there is suffering, cauterize it together with fire, then heat the caustics little and much, according to what is good for the place where the disease is located;
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	afterwards cauterize all of it until you are exhausted with the corruption, and there is nothing left of it, so that all that is corrupted is burned up.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the burned areas oil to soothe them with as much as the burns of fire are healed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of onions that generate heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if after three days a healthy scar does not appear, this is good;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, then start cauterizing again on the part that has remained corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this blister should never be cured with water medicine instead of fire cautery;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but all the way fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already spoken about the cure of the acute medicine in division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of onions that come to the tips
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	For sometimes it happens that at the tips by default a disease is born which is called "close" according to our intention, and it is a large infected thing that bleeds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is according to two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is known as fire cauterization and water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery also is like a pen of a vault, and must be made of good iron to the measure that it can pierce the nail from all sides, and that there are subtle margins;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	after you have put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail as far as it comes to the tip of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and let it stay like this for three days until it begins to move by itself;
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make an ointment of wild mulberries crushed with salt, and let the ointment be on it all night, and the nail will come out and will be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the infected area with poultices until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by many delays of the heart, and often happen to the hands and feet, it is necessary that you bring them fire cautery.
et est en teil maniere:	and in this way:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a nail of iron or steel, or a feather of pigeon, and put it on the claw and the toe, that is to say, to cure warts.
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and put the nail on it so that it burns all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand firm, and press your hand in turning so that the margin of the nail comes to the root of the claw, and may find the hot water way deep to the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and suffer the patient a little pain of the hot water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave it in that state, and it will come off at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Make an after another, as long as you draw out all those who are in the body, then cure the pains that generate heat.
li cure dou trembler	the cure of shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When there is a trembling from cold, or fever, or any other illness, then you must make four cauterizations or three on the spine of the back and one between each spine.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one at the feet, and one on the stomach with olive oil cauterization;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	if it will stop shaking, and quickly heal from cold illness.
des pustules puans	pustules that emit pus
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No one appears on the body by way of sweat, or pustules that emit pus, which come from corrupt humors.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	If it is necessary for the first time that cauterization be made on each head of the pimple:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a fine tip from a fir branch, so that it catches fire, or from a root of arzila long, or with a spherical cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And never make the cauterization at the beginning, according to this method, and they cannot grow anything bad before that, but the excess is broken off, and they are healed;
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it is necessary that this is done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	 often occurs great disturbances of blood from the artery that is cut to the wound that comes to the surface, or incision of the abscess, or cautery of the member, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a very bitter thing to smell.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And whenever one has any, if you quickly put your index finger on the vein wound, and strain it as much as the blood is quietened by your finger, and that drop no longer comes out;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then set on fire the olive oil caustic with small and large ones as long as they are all red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take some, or large or small according to the wound and its location, considering that the artery is cut, and put the caustic on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the caustic in place until the blood is stopped;
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if he pricks when you lie on your back, and the cauterization has ended, then take another of the cauterizations that are in the fire quickly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not stop doing one after the other until the sun is extinguished.
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is dear, and that another ill will not come upon the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and know that when the sun is cut short of the artery, one cannot well stop it flowing even if the artery is large, unless by one of the four ways that we have said:
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by fire cautery, or by extraction when it is not yet treated, or by a strong knot of thread, or by medications put on which have the power to stop the flow;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and let him lie and be held fast together.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who can bring about a good healing of him tightly bound in fabrics or placing burning things on, or other similar things, if it does not help, then do not do it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to anyone and he has neither seen nor applied medicine, then he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and hold it tightly until it is stopped flowing on the wound and on the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move his back, but wet it with cold water often as long as the sun is hot so that it freezes and thickens and hardens.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make incisions in front of those who need cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the remedies for surgery.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases where fire cauterization, burning medicines, and the causes and instruments and forms of cauterization are needed;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have put that head of the shoulder on the ground, and I will go through this chapter in this middle way for those who are dislocated more lightly than those who are broken;
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so since I have begun to speak of this, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of the cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you that you do not undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in the manner of men come in cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	where there are people who have so much fear of their disease that they die easily from the effort of trying to get rid of it, and from the great magnitude of their illness;
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and from these we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And from these I will tell you the story, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am old;
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not appropriate that you grant consent to those who come to you with this behavior, but rather put more trust in your honor than in your convenience, and do not open widely but carefully from him of whom you are certain, and from whom you might have received something and taken it at a distance;
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use divination and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and who will help you achieve great renown, glory, and memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and justice, and if you will, may you seek the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter in discussing by chapters, according to that which is before or the chapter of the cauterizes, which I have devised from the head down to the feet, so that you may find more easily that of which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The water is full of taste.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	I know that this disease often occurs in children when the child's throat is too strongly constricted.
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and it never happens because of a repeated response, which one cannot predict.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this disease affect anyone but children, and all those who have it die quickly;
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for me it seems that I should be more careful in performing the treatment.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose shoulder was swollen with fluid, and whose head grew heavy each day until it could no longer be supported;
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and he believed that he was dying because the moisture had gathered so much that it entered between the skull and the bone, between the jaw and the bone;
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and if they are such that the moisture is between the joint and the bone, and the abscesses are small, then you shall split through the head a wide split;
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and so far as we, until the moisture runs;
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and put this in the form of a spikelet:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the manner of a cross according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is out of the bone, and you see the signs that the head of the spine is split on each side, and the liquid jumps out when you press it with your hand, and it does not close back down:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then you shall split through the head three splits according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract the moisture all at once.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After, hold the splits covered with cloth and powder, and put wine and oil on it, and leave it like that until the fifth day;
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then let it dry out, and cure the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head be extracted evenly, and give the patient dry meat that does not have moisture as much as the member is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is that you look at where the large size of the abscess, and the gathering of the sharp.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	For it is never before;
aucune fois derrier;	it is never behind;
aucune fois en destre;	it is never on the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	it is never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	So size where the abscess opens, and the filling of the sharp, and do as you can do it;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and guard against covering the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and give him blood, so that the patient dies of blood loss and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	In conclusion...
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	If a person has a disease called "cough," and the illness is old, and the benefit of medicine is not there, then the final remedy is to cauterize with what they will block the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It is therefore necessary, when you see them covered, for the patient to raise his head;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	afterward rub the neck with a rough cloth until the arteries are visible, and then extract the patient's collar from all the cloth;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look at where the vein enters, and their leys [veins] from one side to another are after the ears, and few are answered.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then mark the veins at the nape of the neck, and cut them both from one side to another with a small chisel  [spatumile] until the bone is reached, and that may be done by means of a broad chisel at the back of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, bottle the sperm of cows from the vein and the skin above, carving too much like I should on a tree.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is cut, let it flow continuously upwards without stopping.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery is not felt at the touch, then you must measure the quantity of space of three fingers, and then sign the nape and cut to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	And if it is necessary to put the blood on fire then there are six inches [6/8 inch], and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repetition of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If it remains on the bone of the sciatic joint, if the copes that aposteme [abcess] don't come out, then extract the wound and wrap it up, and the treatment of the wound until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of grinding
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old man's hair begins to gray, and he has catarrh due to the moisture of tears and heat in his temples and aged skin and similar things, he is treated with medicine by means of remedies for medicines and none of them benefit him, if we extract the arteries from his temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the method of extracting them is that the patient makes his hair grow again on his temples, and hears the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is not too quickly extracted except in some men who are too cold;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	And if it is extracted, then the patient removes his clothes, and rubs the place with no rough cloth, and raises the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly;
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the sputum of where this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then peel the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then tie it up tightly like pinches, and remove the webbing that are between each part of it;
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if his arteries are thin, then turn it to the point of the hook, and then cut off that part according to the quantity of II shoulders.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not covered, then does not save all in all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And treat the blood of the VI /, until III;
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if his arteries are large, then you must thread them with a strong double silk thread, so that blood does not come out before the wound is healed, and comes out again after the blood has come out;
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then cut off the surplus that is between the two threads at that same moment, and then, if you see it, with the cautery cutellaire, as far as the bone as soon as the shoulders are cut;
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and that is the operation, if the patient does not have a fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cauterization is done to end the moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For by fire it is more helpful against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	For in the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the place with fine cotton cloth and put it on well-made tents;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are removed, let there be dry medicine that makes a chime, and of tents, until he is well;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and without any wound of the artery as you perform it, if you hasten to cover it with fire, or you employ the place of vitriol and extract it with your hand so that the wound is closed;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have fire present, if you put your finger on the place until the wound is frozen, and dip the place in cold water again and again, and extract it as it should be done;
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and the one that is wet and lighter in weight for the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein from both sides, but let the cutting be well done so that it lasts longer on heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instrument is too soft, then it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And there should be between the two knives one inch of space, and then when you have tied up the two ends, and you rub hot iron on it until it comes out to the bone, and cut the vein in two places;
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and be separated between the two shoulders because it is not souded with this fire cauter of all things;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	this is the form of the cauter:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes come down from the veins that are on the forehead of the head of fire, and it does not benefit from medicine that is done to it, and you see the face of the patient turn black, and feel a feverish tremor as if it were shivering;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and the oil is tenacious and moist so that the hair of the scales falls off, and the scales are burned, and scorched by the heat of the tears, so it is necessary to have this cure;
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they called it the ancient "cure for cuts", and this is what you do to the patient who has this disease on his or her hair: make three cuts even along the length of the forehead.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and one of the cuts should also be like two, all the way down to the forehead until it reaches just below the nose, and the other two cuts are on either side of the forehead above the temples, and you must not cut into any arteries that are above the temples.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and remove your hand from the lower part of the two mandibles, and each wound should have three doses joined together;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have ready a sponge and motted cloths to wipe away the blood, then dip the sponge in both sides of this form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision that is supposed to be on the temple until the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape off all the flesh that is between the two cleavages entirely to the bone, and then do the same from the first incision until the second, and then draw out this blade forcibly.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you add water to the first cut of the instrument called 'charnel', and it is very sharp on one side, and soft on the other, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the edge of the cutting tool toward the cheek at the corner, and let the edge be soft toward the bone, and dip it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And scrape off all the scales that descend from the head to the flesh until the incision is continuous up to what opens at the cleavage, and then do the same in the middle cut until the other side;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw out the blood evenly, and press on the vein so that the blood comes out;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	and then put in each cut a tent of wet linen, and place drapes soaked with wine and oil and vinegar on them, and watch so that the abscesses do not leak;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and for the third day let him lie in bed, and I will bring a great amount of fresh water, then the remedy with basilicon oil mixed with rosewater, and other remedies that are used to heal wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	To keep hair long and even.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When there is no catarrh by habit, and you see the hairs thin and short, and weakening of sight, and burned paper.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and where it grows in there is sharp pain in the patient, and he coughs up phlegm;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Therefore, because of these accidents, it is clear that this matter and this catarrh do not come from many veins, but from one; and the remedy that is given to him, if it is this one, then it is right.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to rub his forehead, then make a deep incision in his forehead, and another one from left to right.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begins with the incison on the left temple to the right temple, and be the incision up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when one chews;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, so suck all the blood with a sponge, and then tie between the two lips of the incision and put cotton wool, and bandage it with linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	and then hang them over a drape soaked in wine and oil, and keep them warm from the abscess.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is extracted, if you rub the bone as much as it begins to bleed, then treat it with dried things, which cause dry matter to form.
En teil maniere:	In this way:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take 2 parts of flour from bread, and 3 parts of colophony, and make an ointment;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	And apply it to these wounds to cause dry matter to form everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the bumping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All those who have an ear are one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grain, or beast, or a small stone, or similar thing as iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, if like peas, beans, or peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing thing if like water and easy to move, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it is in the ear a stone or some other thing that does not fit into the ear, and does not enter it, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, if there is no drop of violet oil or oil of sweet marjoram, then apply extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and let it sweat from heat, and it stops the nostrils when the sweating comes, and puts around the ear pieces of linen or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and let the ear be up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Mouth times a great remedy comes;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out strongly, then he is given extraction with subtle pincers, for the form is:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes out strongly with the pincers, it is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then extract with the small sharp tool;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if not with the sharp tool, then make a small hole in the ear canal or pierce the ear lid firmly, and stop the one who is inside the canal with soft wax so that it does not come in with the cannula;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then let him sweat strongly, for many times it comes out strongly as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come in some way, so take the glans, and place in some certain instrument that is right for this, and put a little cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glans on stone or something, and practice well.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come out with all of these things we have said, then you must hurry to cut the ear in such a way that the abscess comes out and spasm;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the way of the cut if you do first save the patient from the head injury, and remove the blood according to the measure of its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear up, and make a small cut at the root of the ear onto the fat or where it depends;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the cut be like a moon, as far as you come to the stone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it gently into your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the treatment as long as he is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is a tooth that hurts and swells, then administer an extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if he cannot spit, then administer a thin spit-like substance according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and incise that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not use this when you think that the tooth is moist due to moisture in the ear, as many times as you have used it;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with thin tweezers and with a pick, as we have said, so that the extractions are ordered.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water, then, when he spits in his ear, the patient should use an elder's cough first, and widen the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And be careful about that ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it falls there, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	Or if not, then take several pearls according to the length of your finger and make them light, and heat them a little by the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put the patient a little pearl in his ear, and cut off one of his other teeth, and fix it with another stone on the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease to make a stone on top of a stone until the water comes out completely, and so it all jumps up completely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, then take one joint, and dip one of the ears in water, and the other head burn with fire until the longer joint is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then make another part of other joints until the water comes out completely, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the arrow, if it is a small one, like a flea or a similar thing, treat it as we have said in the dislocation.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is a big one that can be felt, then arrange for the extraction of pincer-type things;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the dislocation and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then you must look at the ear towards the sun;
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there is no opening, if the trail is small pinches, and if it does not open, take the grip of where this is the shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it must be tight below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And pour out the thinnest chief in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck all the form:
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often as much as the whole blood comes.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not submit to be taken out, then stop it with cotton in the ear as I said in the stone:
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out as we have said, administer distillations that the old ones have tried in the extraction of worms, and you will find them or the treatment of the distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distil your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, where this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And of silver or gold are you made, of small holes, and above them for distillation.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press into the instrument of silver made well for this, and you take the razor and wrap cotton around the tip facing forward;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then you pour your oil or juice, and what you take of your medicines in the line, and the line is in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then pour into the razor all of the cotton, and press your hand slightly while distilling or moving the oil out of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient smells inside, and the distillation is a little heated like this so that it is distilled in the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and keep it from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the bumping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have small holes in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and these same things happen to the ears because of the piercing of a wound or of a needle going into the ear, and this piercing sometimes comes out completely from the ear, so that one cannot see it.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and never does the hole go deeper than the eye can see.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which has come out completely, so that one cannot see it, is a serious wound for many people, and in this case, you should put the patient's ear in the sun.
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the operation clearly, if the wound has already been cleansed of its pus, and here is the shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And be smooth and clean in front and behind, so that it doesn't hurt the ear.
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the wound is a needle or a pin stuck in the ear, if there are only few small wounds, and clean it lightly, until the needle is completely out.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the swelling is completely in the ear, then take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly on the fire, and then put the bar of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the swelling that causes the patient earache, then do so lightly and be careful not to injure the ears.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then put in the ear a small piece of felt according to its size, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do not do this every day until the wound is healed, but take a small piece of felt and moisten it with rosewater, and powder with vitriol brew.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear drain, so that you take out the felt and remove another felt moistened with rosin oil, which is made of rosewater and wax, until the swelling has subsided;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the pain comes, dip a sponge and a cloth in cold water and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that the doctor uses to relieve the pain which are or to treat the distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper pile
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	Apply hot water to the hair when they are moist and dry, so that you pull them with nail files and tweezers, and cut off a small piece of their roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	And then put on top of the vinegar.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it is not peeled, then the fire cautery, with the subtle lens-shaped cautery, and the fire cautery after incision makes the muscles move.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often repairs, so that nothing remains attached to its roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are cauterized with fire, if the roots are burned and do not return again.
de la gresle	of the grate
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often come in papers some hairs that seem like grumous things in their form and dureness, and for this reason this disease is called "grinald", and is a mass of moisture thick in the paper on top and inside;
li ovraiges est telz:	The treatment is as follows:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	take care that the grinald moves from one side to the other, and this is a light thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	do the fire on each side in turn, then scorch it lightly, then take it with pincers and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cover it without piercing a little bit of paper, then do not harm the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the break is large, then join it with a stitch, and heal as long as it is healthy;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, then do not use force, for with time and without force, it will heal itself and cause a scar.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the piercing goes from the outside of the ear towards the top, then turn the paper over and pierce it with tweezers, and cover and press from both sides;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is moved by the incision, then do not harm.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the piercing is covered, let it be oiled with salty water, and heal the place where it causes a scar as long as the patient remains healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinch is a grease that is caught in the webs of paper on top of it, and this happens more often to children than to adults, and grieves them much, and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hurry to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And so when they lie down on their faces, and sleep on it, and their paper is wet above their chins which swells and changes color because of the Exinch that forms in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place between your two arms and feel the pain between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the way of this treatment is that the patient puts his head in salt water;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then he takes a linen cloth, and sets up a tent in the form of a circle according to the quantity of Exinch in each part, and then puts it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your hands from both sides so that the Exinch is assembled into the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	And cut into the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula, making a split that is not larger than the wound made to the vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin smooth all the way until you come out.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in many places it comes out of the split, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	So remove all the bandage between your two hands at the end, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is well spread out.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and keep your hands from touching the split, so that you do not come into contact with all of the spatula up to the oil, so that you do not dirty it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the extraction does not come out in the tightness of the split, so that the split is slightly opened, just a little;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then, as we have said, then take out with care, then moisten the wrappings in water, and put them back on, and draw from the bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind salt and put on it to corrupt that moisture which is delayed.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal him as long as he is healthy.
