Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of an abscess, then the healer pours water and soothes it as long as he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hair from papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hair grows on paper that is not natural to it, and becomes wrinkled, if it damages the hairs, and causes certain diseases as usual tears and softening of the papers and scabs, so much that it is a cause of hair destruction;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and is the cure according to four ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by fire cautery, or by medicine astringent according to that which it is before, or by plaster of cautery, and is made or by incision and stitching or by cutting, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the disease in your right hand, then turn the paper of oil to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	s'elle est convertie, c'est boin;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if it is converted, that's good; if not, pour an aiguille on all the thread above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let this be the margin of the paper where the hairs grow out from these hairs, and lead the thread above all the paper, and turn it back to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the dislocated part of the paper, dislocating the hairs, all the spine completely covering, from the big tear until the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then remove the thread, and place on the paper a little piece of cloth and drape, then sign on the paper a shape like a pear, as if it were a mirth, and moreover, the shape must be according to the quantity that you want to lift up the paper which is devised to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if it is necessary that much of the paper be lifted according to what you have determined, so that the paper softens;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	and then stretch out all the spine on the two lines that you have marked, and start with great pain until small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let it be one of the cleavages near the hair in the thickness of a root, then pour the vinegar into one of the two angles where cure, and then scorch it all;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then join the two lips to a stitch of a needle with very fine thread, and wash the blood, and make air the excess of the threads on the two loops at nothing sticky, if you see to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, if you are not cured, then leave the stitch and the threads until three days or four;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound without a stitch of drying and constricting things, for the paper is relieved at the sound of the wound and the gathering of it, but the stitch is dead (as the old say), and it is painful work;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	is that you sign the paper with a mold that is also like the fur of mirabene, as we have told, at three times you will reverse it according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	and then chop off who is raised to small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the tweezers, and the thing is not even, take a needle with a thread, and sew the shape:
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and bottle another delicate thread, and the second strong, and the third small, and join together between your two threads evenly:
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then move your hand evenly, and then cover all the skin with which you have signed, as we have told, then join together the two lips of the wound with a stitch, and treat it until it is well;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, so that the pain is relieved by a poultice and similar soothing ointment;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and never has it happened that the hair of the paper is converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if you use what we said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitch between the two is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of wounds is done according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and you turn the paper and put it inside according to what I said, and then make two incisions by art, and two sutures very long as the paper is and as narrow as the thread that is used for the sponge.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and tie like two shoulders on each side where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then join them very gently over what rises from the paper by oil, and strain the two incisions of the two parts together;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it like this for a few days, and the wound that was drained will get better and heal on its own,
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is late, if the cup has one force, then heal it as long as it is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is sewed up, and if the paper is lifted up, and they will no longer feel the hair;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two claws that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The ovraige is such that you press a very fine needle, and you pour a very fine and subtle silk thread;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then join the claws together very subtly, and make the length of the threads one palm's length of yarn;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then arrange the other thread of fine silk briefly, and tie the claws with a very subtle thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then place the patient's head in your seat;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	And let the sun be bright so that the ovraige is subtle and small, then pour the needle into all of the hair at the root, and make it go through the paper quickly as you draw it up from the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull out the hair up to the jaw, pour it into the jaw, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then pull your hand out so that the hair comes all the way out to the jaw in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the jaw is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then draw the jaw back with all the thread you have ordered, so that the jaw comes out from the hole above and you can see it with the eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	then draw back the jaw and the thread, and when the oil comes out and leaves it for two or three days, let the hair grow in its place and the hair grows on top of it;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hair is short, then accompany a long natural hair with it, and lift it up or leave it, so that it is extended and then let it lie down.
de la porriture de l’oil	to prevent oil damage
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	Now this disease, which is called "bleeding," or where the poultice comes in contact with oil, there are two ways.
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and another unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And there is a doubt and fear about injury, or a cut, or a cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of treatment in this is that you tear away the skin, and separate the lips from it, and put linseed inside, and keep it until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and you should not use for the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the disease will come back worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but treat with things that soften, as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the water of the spring or the ale be boiled, and the seed of flax be cooked, and the oil of dill be melted in none of the oils, and wrap it up, and treat with it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your remedy is that you put yourself on guard so that it does not harden according to the shape that it was before.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and the remedies that we have said are only effective if we address this disease, so that it does not return according to the shape that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the horse that comes out of the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is called "axacrati," is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wounds and slashes and cauterization and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of this chapter is that you take a needle, in which it has double thread, and throw it into the flesh, and pierce it with the left hand so much to the right, that the thread comes out at II shoulders of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then put the hook above all the needle, and the cap above the wide spike.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what it should, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If he does not, take the razor and put it in the split, and turn the paper over, and make two splits where it sits inside the paper.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the two splits of the two angles of the incision that you have made be joined together so that when they are put together, their shape is like the shape of a letter which has no «I griesche».
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then cut off that piece, according to the quantity that its sides are apart, from that which is inside the paper, then attach the two separated parts, and sew them together with a thread of linen;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then use the medicines that we have spoken of to soften it, and wrap it up, until it is well.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a split, or a stitch, or a cauterization, then it is necessary that you make a straight split in the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said above;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and it must be done the preparation according to the form of the disease, for it is many different in form, and the master surgeons order everything so that it may return to its natural form;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is required for preparation and instruments in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	doux soudain de la papier
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this weld is made in such a way that the paper above is welded with the white of oil, and cannot move or perform its natural work, then it is necessary that you should burn the tip of a razor on the paper, and blow it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and spread them out as pinches, until you have what is suitable for the subtle spaulding, which should not be too sharp or too fine, so that the patient does not suffer from the too sharp spaulding which might blister the oil;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and so your incision, from which you peel off the gathered one, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it is healed all that has been gathered, and does not go into the sharp salt water, and the lifting of the soft water, and the chain;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and put on the oil wool wet in abundance of ointment;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days use the chain and the dry things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the finger is according to two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	she is nervous and seems to I dry medicine, and another that is not at all nervous, but seems to be white frozen moisture, which when you touch it with iron and heat it with pinches, so can't anyone;
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both appearances begin to spread towards the great tears, and grow less and less until they cover the whole sight and light and motion of oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the way of incision is that the patient puts his head in your lap, then he works on the hairs;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and give the paper to your hand, and twist the fingernail with small tweezers, and lift them up;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put a hair of horse, or cow, or bull, and thread it firmly;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the needle's point slightly and thread it through the nail, and pierce it completely through the nail, and tie the nail with a thread and lift it up, and peel off all the nail that remains on the toe of the nail where the pluck comes out and the silk on the hair until the head, then cut the remaining one in the root of the tears with an incision very thin and small, and leave the natural tears or tears usually come; so that by the incision does not go the course of the tears:
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and never stretch the finger at the knuckle alone, and on the wire, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then burn it all off with fire so that this is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And keep so that the spindle does not touch the raw wool and tear it, and that the needle is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision pour a little oil of sesame, and a ring made of limestone, and leaves it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then he cares for this as much as it is healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the finger is not nerveous, and you cannot put in the needle, and this shape of the joint with medicines is cured many times;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they are born as I have told you in the division, and if you see it covered, so work with oil of sickness, and take a light spindle according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And raise the finger slowly, and if you see it slim down little by little and its root is pressing hard, then distil from your mouth in the oil collar made of litargyrum and dou collar red and brown, and stop the oil until the next day.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then begin again with this same work, as much as it is all boned.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If any thing is opposed to oil in the flesh, as an abscess is, then milk, and first treat the abscess while it is sound, then begin again the work as before until it is sound.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	If the appearance of the flesh of the arm hurts in the oil, then suspend it for a moment, and dip some part of it, not all at once, so that tears do not come;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distil in the red oil collar which is made of litargyrum.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh that grows on the apricot
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	Some men have never had a red hair, and they peel the prunelle and bind it to papers and turn it towards the sun, and seem like a rose of basil.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the head-injury if the patient places his head in your lap, then he turns the eyes, and twists all this in the shape of a hook with appropriatehooks, and supports it with force;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first layer, and keep cutting all the way to the end, and be careful not to blight the oil at the head-injury;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and be the incision of the spatumile that we have said in the incising of the nail and with small efforts so that one oste the sebene, if like the form after this chapter shows it;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the bone is cut, then employ the oil of seil or you distill colier red and similar medicines corrosive, and put on the oil a cotton with admixture of ointment, so that it is assured of an abscess heated;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if I do not delay, and the sun rises, and you doubt an abscess, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with things that calm an abscess;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and then return to your work as long as it is healthy, and in this way make a paste that is mixed with oil by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But first you should know that you should adjust the cure of each weak oil according to the natural path;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental way, in iron work;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that the members are suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the hairs
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	are red that are covered on the oil, and endure his work and weaken the oil all the time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	So the first thing you should know is that if you see that the oil is good, healthy, and strong, and there is no other disease than health;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then mix it with some water in this way:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Tell the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins completely according to his wisdom, and let the incisions be subtle twice as much according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And are two oils by degrees in one degree according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	Then bind those veins with care, and wash the blood every hour another one, until you see remove those veins away from the oil;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and keep that you do not blur the oil at the tips of the needles, and make this work before noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you don't overheat those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, if distill in the oil green and red essence to corrupt what is delayed of the stink;
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you do not have the power to bind all of that in this hour, then make a plaster on the oil of soothing things for the pain of the hairs, and leave it for several days until the pain is relieved and assured of an abscess being hot, then begin again according to this method which is before until he is healthy;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of healing:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the pipe
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The wound is called a fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you treat it with fire cautery and medicinal herbs as I have described above, and it is not healed, then cut open the abscess at the root, where it must die, and drain all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you will see corruption and blackness, then this is the form:
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called an "aspire chief", and be done from head to foot, and be poked as with a nail as it is in this form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the corroded part of the bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press with your hand a little until you feel that corruption has been removed:
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do not make this again, then return to the place of medicine drying.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the leather is tight, and it has not been washed for a while, and the core of the bow is also tight, and remains so for 40 days, and there is no sign of an abscess, and other bad things do not happen, then he is healthy.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, if there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula to the perforation of the nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone the second time with iron, and with medicines that dry, and when it is uncovered take care that the iron is at three angles, and the furrow is smooth until the top, as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then put it on the bone with the limb, and keep your hand away from the oil I pick, then turn all the iron until it pierces the bone and the patient feels pain according to what he experiences when holding his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and when you restore the place of dry medicine, as I have taught you, and when the horse becomes hot and toughens the limbs, then bring the matter to the nose.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	is less burdensome for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When all limbs are open everywhere, and there is no disturbance to the nose, nor reduction, if it comes that you lay the patient down;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the healer, then put leechers there to suck without hurting to extract, then put on oil, made from acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocollus, and then strain the oil, and apply it with bandages and sheets;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the sheets that you take enough soft sheets, and double each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the limbs need;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	and then extract from above a hard bandage, and start again the suction to avoid hurting;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the suction cups and leave the oil extracted day and night, and it softens over time, so you must remove it all;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the bandage after day and night, and if you see the oil heal, it is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then start again with the plaster and linen, and the bandage and suction cups until it is well.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the breaking of a thread from a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When the dislocation comes in the wrapped cloth, then open it, and comes out like grains of resin, and is likely to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it covered, the wrappings are such that you stick a needle into the root of the part below until it comes out at the top, and then stick another needle where there is thread from the arm;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cover the head of the thread with a double thread and tie a part of the vein, and tighten it well, then remove the needle and put another oil in abundance of vinegar;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread rubs against the vein, then heal the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the wound is never restricted by the vein in any part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the hairs are of great appearance, if he pierces it with a fine spud that comes perfectly from the oil, and drives away the moisture of the albuginea and cuts the hairs, and enters again so soon;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "Alcunnati" does not exist except in oil, resembling water descending, and it is not water;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of this appearance of the opening is that you make sit the patient on one seat dressed and straight, then take the head between your two hands, and move it while you see the bow come up to your hair.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let him lie down, and do not get up or be upset, and look at the patient's things so as he wanted.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not get up, know that it is acute, and the moving of the bow should not be dressed as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	if you sit the patient between your hands, then take the thin spatulum and set it on the corneal membrane I spot by the continuance of the connection with the corneal membrane and the crown, until the bow comes out.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is out, if it is mixed with hot liquid honey, or sharp water or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then be cured by another cure as long as it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have sharp tools in our division, and what is needed to pierce.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	If we work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you put the patient in a cross-legged position between your hands, away from the light of the sun, and press firmly on him with oil.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then put the oil paper in your left hand if the hairs are on the left, or in your right hand if the hairs are on the right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand, if the hairs are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the hairs are on the right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument at the center of the hair by its thickness with a rakes of oil on the part of the smaller wound, then press the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and turn your hand back until it pierces in the oil's blubber, and feel that almagda comes to the hollow thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and the measure of the vein of the eye must be at the perfect end of the space that is from the apricot up to the end of blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	is the crown of oil;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	you will see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the transparent horn, and put the instrument up to the eye where the water is, then express it out one way at a time.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he is now sitting down, then see the patient in front of him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	Then rest for a little while, and the water comes up again, put pressure on it with the instrument, and when it is firmly in place, gently extract the eye turning your hand this way and that;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put a little drop of gem water in it, and remove this oil from inside it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place by the side the oil of spikenard or another moist oil in a cup and in plenty of wine, and mix with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are of our group, let us put on quickly with plenty of wine.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the almagre cannot enter into the oil because of its hardness, since there are some men who have very hard hairs, then you must squeeze the instrument which is called "alberit", from which comes this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And so pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make a small hole then drop in the water, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and when the work is finished, prepare for the patient a dark place to sleep, where he sleeps on his back.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be free from all movement, and eat light food, and do not move his head to the right or left, and tie him according to his condition for three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then remove it in the same dark house and test his sight, and let him see a few things, and then he is tied again until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and do not do this while the patient is still suffering from the incision, but it is necessary to keep him quiet, so that the blood does not flow.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	For the abscesses, when they are ready, you must remove the dressing before the seventh day and clean them up.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when he is calmed down, so that the sight turns inward and sets on his cheek, let it hang down all day, and be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then take him out of the house little by little, and turn him around.
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no one should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us from the Land of Jerusalem who told us that in their country they still made almagre by grinding, for which they sucked the water, but I have never seen any such thing in our country, nor have I ever heard of it in books of the ancient ones.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the appearances of the shapes of almagre, so that he who does not know them may see them.
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let there be pure copper:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this middle substance be, and behind it in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	from the chest to the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	No time are born or are diverse eggs eggs laid, of which there are some who seem scorpions at mouth pies;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such eggs or if there is an egg with green color and if there is an egg with good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In this case of these eggs that is green, and not encrusted, it is convenient that you seat the patient between your hands towards the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and apply the egg to those eggs, and dry them firmly;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then take this that you can hold in your hand of a fine blade made of iron from one side, as long as you see that this egg is all bone;
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains nothing of it that cannot be covered, if you open it with all the delicate instruments lightly, so that nothing stays;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if he does not soar up, or an abscess, so much sear as it is necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize as soon as the sweat is dried up and all the pus is drained, then apply oil or vinegar to the wound immediately and thoroughly.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If it has been operated on, and moisture enters as far as the palate, know that he is healthy;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not penetrate so much as it should, know that there is no bone above it, and the instrument will not cut properly:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then you must insert a piece of linen thread that is neither too thick nor too thin, and wind it around each knot with enough space or less between them as needed;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and place the patient's head on the thread so that it supports his weight, and draw it by the nose while smelling so that it comes through his nose into his mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times teach the child to use the pot, and this is a light thing for him who must do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	and then take the head that comes by the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and tie them together in turn while we are spinning like this.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Make it so that you can hear that the new one has been corrupted, then treat the thread, wash the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian salt, and then put it back on the nose as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Make it so that you can hear that the oil has been corrupted for three or more days, as long as the thread is delayed from the car;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on the nose a string of linen for some days as long as it is healthy, and if there is a need to use dried medicines, do so.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, whereon one distills oils and medicines or severs.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And be of silver or gold, resembling a lamp open, as a chain, and conduct it also;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, then make a closed chain, and be the instrument plain for purging the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and I always hold the head when one heats oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the chest to the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a pain arises in the head from a disease called "thunder", and increases and becomes great enough that it is visible with the eye;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And for this you must kop it at the beginning, and the bone all over, then put fire on the cautery or medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay koping it until it is great, then take care if it is hard, of its color, of its poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	If one does not touch iron, for it is an abscess that is inflamed, because when it is touched there comes great evil to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	And if the abscess is caused by a soft touch, not by a sharp object, and you see that it can be covered completely, then empty the patient and cover it without fear, and heal the place with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and sewed up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Saiches that when solu[t]ions of continuance comes into one of these ovraiged cartilage, i profit poc, fur that in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary that there be no doubt if the wound is fresh throughout;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two lips with a stitch, and then heal it as long as it is healthy;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are twisted on one side or the other, then it is necessary that you peel all the parts of their skin as long as they heal, and then join the two lips with a stitch, and tighten them, and powder them with dragon's blood and burnt incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the powders a piece of plaster from strong or other plaster that bonds, and leaves it until it falls by itself, then heal with ointment as long as he is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method for suturing is that you assemble the solution thus:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the method for suturing the abdomen;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	With hands at home inside the lips of an abscess seem like grains of sand, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn the lips, and cut each notch, and take it with pincers and cut it into each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and then apply the vitriol paste after the incision, until the scar is stained;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it rest, and heal the wound with dry things as long as he is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the cheeks
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times, he comes down on the gums with a sharp edge, which the old people call "albula".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	If it is convenient that you hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and let the bow or blood run;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then put thereon the vitriol powder, or other restraining and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it returns after the incision, and often happens, so that when you cut it again, and cauterize it;
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the instruments for copping.
des sordens	of the ordains
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	No times are assembled at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, sharp and rough things;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and no times are the teeth black and yellow and rotten, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	If it is necessary that you hold the sick person between your hands, and his shoulders are in your presence, and you lift up the lower parts or the buttocks that protrude, as long as there is nothing to delay it;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and do so with black and green, and yellow and other colors, until they are all mixed together;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one does not take the first cut, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have all lifted up;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth have to do with different kinds of tools for grinding, according to what the doctor demonstrates, because the rasier used to remove the hair from between the teeth is of a different shape than that which grinds the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these shapes and others are fitted with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you cure a tooth of its pain that you draw it out as soon as possible, for this must not be done at all.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a high-quality substance, so there is no excuse to delay drawing it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	So then when the patient is in pain, you must be certain of the toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often the pain of the patient disappears, and he believes that it is in a good tooth, and he makes the tooth that hurts him be pulled out;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not go away for this, until the evil is extracted, because we have already done it to these patients;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are sure of the tooth that hurts, then it is necessary that you scratch the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gums on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then you put it in your hand or in small pliers very carefully at the first hole and hole, until it is well extracted, then he grasps the pliers firmly;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the sick person between your knees, and hold it still very well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not fall out on its own, take one of these instruments and gently place it inside each part, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if his nose is pierced and bleeds, then you should fill it with gauze, where the piercing is;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if he is held with subtle tongs so that he does not break when he is extracted;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to cover the wound on the gums in order to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you must take care not to break it, and if a part remains, and return it to the patient by the wickedness of the root, causing greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And be careful that you do not do it like the ignorant surgeon who, because of his haste and recklessness, often breaks the carriage, and does not administer what we have told you;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but bring it once by the root of that great disease so that it does not hold on to anything, or by the carriage that it breaks, as we have often wanted;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the heat is removed, wash its place with wine or sesame oil and linen.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and when it heals over, so that often happens, if you employ the place of vitriol crushed;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if it does not work, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments, so that the teeth first move slowly, are long and thick, so that they do not double up when you draw the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick members so that they do not bend when you pull it, and let them be of good forged iron, and let them have teeth for holding it in place.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in place at the extraction, if you put cotton wet with oil or butter on the place for one or two days until the roots are soft, since the claws that are called "algefri" seem like a fingernail;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and inside make it as with a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you should strip the flesh completely around the root, and put the instrument that is called 'althali', that is to say file, which is this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be big or small so that it does not break, and its root springs up from this, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, if you aid yourself with all the instruments, whereby the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two heads, from which this form comes:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the rationale of the dens, and from this instrument which seems like a pair of large pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	and let the instrument be big so that it cannot break, and know that many of the thick instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the master sagacious tries his instrument himself according to what his work and the disease demonstrate to him, because there are many diseases for which the old do not teach instruments, but if it does not break the carriage or other bones on which it rolls, or on which he is laying, if he seeks the instruments that are appropriate to it, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, whereby this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and strong holding to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but it can hold and cut off.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place of the medicines that fit this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, if the doctor has all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not straight according to the natural shape of the body, and the form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the root is not beyond the tooth, and is not in its right place, and can not be sewn or filed.
adonques lou raie;	then the extract:
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is aerated with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is similar to a small needle, and made of iron as it were:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits tight and tight to the tooth's durezza, and so that you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, then take a file of this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file where we make needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and by little and little he pulls his teeth out, so that it does not move until it makes a sound.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and then smooth it all down with a rasp, and its hardness is too great and it blisters the tongue, so it is necessary to sharpen the razor until it is even, so that it does not blister the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth moves
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the teeth are loose in front, whether by pounding or by biting, and the patient cannot press on what he is chewing so that he does not make noise, and you have cured them of constricting medicines, and that does not help;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if it is necessary to restrain it with a gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and rotten, but the gold does not move at all;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you want to put in place the teeth, take the wire and double bottle between the two teeth healthy, then put the heads between the teeth of meat, if there is one or more, until you have cleanly up until the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	and then start again with the covering up until the part where you are starting, and hold your hand gently and cleanly as long as it doesn't move;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your hand be at the root of the tooth so that he can't escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then take the heads with pliers, and assemble them together, and put them between the healthy tooth, and so that he doesn'blece the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if he falls, or the wire breaks, hold it with another wire;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it was to take long, it will last all its time, and this is the shape of the bones and the appearance of the joints of the two upper limbs, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, if it is put back in its place little by little, as we have said:
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And if one is not skilled and patient, and does not do it little by little, and a tooth is put back into the socket, as we have said, and delayed and served thus for a long time;
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the ring of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	And never is it good that comes out of the tongue or nature, which one is born with:
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by an accident of a seared wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and hold his head in your hand, and raise his tongue:
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	and then sever the nerves of the limb as far as the tongue is detached from its bed, and if there is any pain or not, and this is due to sudden injury from a wound, so that he severs the ligature and cuts the nerves;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the cut does not go too deep, lest the artery be severed;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done so, raise the level of the water and thus dry it with linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and let the patient have each night, so that the ligature does not close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if the blood comes out again, put vinegar on the wound;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if it does not stop, then cauterize with the slow fire, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat with other treatments until he is well,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a dark or hard-colored sore that the patient does not feel, do not touch it, for this is a cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining towards the blench, and there is moisture, if he gets the oncine, and he rubs with a thin spatula, and frees it from both sides;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if he comes to your aid, put vinegar on it until it is blistered, and then return to your aid as you draw everything out firmly;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift his arm up and down and stretch it, and cure him with other cures until he is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Once inside the throat are the "goda" which are called mandibles, and they are properly called; when you cure them, as we said in the section on dislocation, and if they are not cured, take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If the abscess is small and its color is pale, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and its root is large, then do not touch it with iron, also for the pain of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it until it has stopped bleeding, and then you will remove it, or it would tear itself apart;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of pale color and its root is thin, then prepare the instrument to cover it, but first look to see if the abscess is hot and inflamed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in the sun and let his shoulders be warm, and let him open the mouth and place the finger between his hands, and press the tongue towards the instrument, so that it is shaped like this:
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and be of silver or of fine gold as well as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	And then press the tongue on all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if take the onion and put it in amber, and try harder than you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and don't try any threads with it, then wrap the instrument, so this is the form, that seems a strong one;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all the time the head are curved, and one side to another, and they are very sharp, and is made of iron where or of anvil:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you take off the cover with pliers, here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be trenchant on one side, and no name on other side;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have copied one of the ambers, if copy the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot water, and very easily, and let it stand until it is well, if gargarize the patient with cooked pomegranate juice, or dried leaves of mirth, and similar things, as much as the sun is set;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then treat until he is well;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and never emerge in the throat other abscesses than the two mandibles, if they are removed as thoroughly as the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was within her throat, namely a small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had very tightly closed all the throat so that the woman could neither breathe nor drink nor eat and would have died if she had stayed like this for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so raised that it had risen two inches on either side of the opening where it was growing.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	So I hurried, and stuck in one of the oesophagi, then pulled it firmly, and pushed a large portion of bowels out;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	and then refitted it again on the other side of the opening of the nose, and shut his mouth and pressed his tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	Afterwards I stuck in the oesophagus into these abscesses, and filled a part of it, and let out only a little bit of blood;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and then cut off the woman's throat, and now began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting that abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess then closed again, and filled up the space that I had emptied, until it became very thick;
