adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I set it in place and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	so that it stopped growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and then I left those parts, and only God knew what would happen to me next.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the wound heals up and the woman runs away and is far away, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if she becomes pregnant and grows fat, she is called "wound".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When she has healed, as we have said in the dislocation, and her healing does not benefit, and you see that the lower abscess is calm and pale, then it is time to cut her.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is roundly assembled and is not far off;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or frothy red or black, so that you avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the eye disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its blenching and its length, that you cause the patient to sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned above;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then you place the onyx in its uvula, and draw it back, and cover it with the two instruments which I have said in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the surplus which is beyond the natural term;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cover more, it will be painful to the voice and to speaking;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use of that which we have said in the incision of the two mandibles, and heal it until it is well.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has doubt about covering, then you must use fire cautery on the sensitive part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of fire cautery is sharp and bitter.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the sick person puts his head in your lap, and then he presses the tongue to the instrument which we have said or fire cautery, and confuses with sharp quick water, so that it is not too thick or too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using the movement of this instrument, from which comes this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And put the head in a cap or hood where the medicine is placed, as if it were the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument on all the medicine on top of the head;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and let the patient lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down his throat and hurt him;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then take your hand to all the medicine and press it on top of the head, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it clear and the medication is gone;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument on all of the cotton on the string above, until the cotton dries on the fabric.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and clean after three or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to re-apply the medicine cauterization, if necessary, and after the cauterization wash out the cotton wrapped around it with water from a vessel, of cotton wetted in the medicine, and clean what is inside of the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be dipped in cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is well.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than the incision, only the cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured with fumigation in this way, take calamus and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and aron and similar herbs, and put them all or any of them into a pot, and pour it in easily, and let it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and may be well glued with strong soil, and enmi the pot has I instrument chisled according to this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And is of silver or gold, and is one of the heads bottle in the mouth of the patient as long as the steam rises through the cannula until the urine is deprived;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the beginning often, as long as the urine is dry, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the opening of the abscess, because many things have come;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and not to make what ever that to the decline of the abscess is hot.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cannula and put inside the head of a hook made of wax, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the hook of wax does not let the steam be heavier in the mouth, and this is a good cure together save.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times there is an obstruction in the throat of bone or spine of fish, or nothing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So if you can see it, you must draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and if what does not open and is put back in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	in case the thing opens up by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or if the patient swallows a sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread crust;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and he lets it hang on a string, and then swallows it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the right place, if it opens, and then draw hard;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come from what we have said, then take this instrument of throwing according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And the instrument is curved at the top so that it can enter the throat more easily and raise the jaw;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it come out, nor poke the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and make sure the patient does not cough up the instrument, so that it does not get stuck or stuck;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if he swallows the instrument whole, or pulls it out smoothly all at once, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	And make the instrument curved at the tip so that it can enter the throat more easily, and raise the chief [larynx] higher; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or else the sound will be blocked, nor should you prod the bone within; and make sure that the patient swallows the instrument, for in doing so he will feel relief or pain; if the fluid is swallowed, or if it is drawn out of the instrument evenly, then let it go.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No medicine will heal him without bloodletting, as I said in the division, by the treatment of medicine;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when that does not help, then look in the mouth of the sick person with the sun, so that you press the tongue to the instrument which I have told you;
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, if it runs with a small hook, or with tiny claws that go under him.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if he doesn't respond, take a dog's chain, and pour it into the throat of the patient, then pour or pour from the chain's iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient's blood is very hot every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	and then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and fill it with water, and move his hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if soon the blood feels the water, let him spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not feel cold as we have said, then fumigate the patient with ash, using the instrument I have spoken of in the smoking treatment.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, because it will soon taste bitter.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	and the method of smoking if it is so that you press the mud or there are coal ashes in a place, and in that same pit there is a hole for the instrument to enter;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then pour the smoke treatment, and let the patient put the head of the cane in his mouth, and close his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape but goes straight to the blood;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the blood will now stop, and if it does not stop, then begin the fumigation again and again;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and suffer the patient to have thirst, and drink no water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then the remedy will be good for him that he should pass through this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the form of the instrument how it passes the blood, if it is so, when one can see it, seems like hooks bent to force them to enter the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has the appearance of a careening beak, and it is sharp like limestone, so that whoever takes it cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and see this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Mouths of appearances of an abscess are, according to what the memory comes here before one and another in this book, and are diverse in perforation and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways, of which one is in its own image, and from that which causes moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	The second way is for the joints where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess at the top is different from that at the root, and the abscess at the shoulder joint is different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if to abscesses one must not pierce, as long as the bowels are still according to their fulfillment;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if to such that one must pierce when they are curbed, and do not die according to their fulfillment, as is the case with abscesses that are deliquescent joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come out of the joints, and are left until they rot within, for fear that if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, then this is a cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or the abscess is from the principal member, and if you delay the perforation as long as it is still alive, it will harm the principal member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or the foundation is deliquescent, if one pierces it so that it is still alive;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not convenient that you pierce an abscess without digestion having been accomplished, so that the foundation, which is deliquescent, does not become completely corrupted, and be dilated within, and a fistula come about;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and can't heal it for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	and you must know the time for the perforation of the abscess which is dead according to the fulfilment, and that is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of fever, and the 감소 of pain and redness, and the movement and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you must make the perforation sit more comfortably in the place of the abscess, and where it opens;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the perforation is long in the body, and the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and sides and all over the body, and there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to which limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in a raised state, if you allow the piercing to remain until it is completely cured, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this, if your body was full of blood from it, and wet with pus;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and because of this they harden the lips and him parboil.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that are pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to which the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must bring a little abscess, a little pit;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in great abscesses, great pits, and many splits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if at such abscesses it is necessary to pierce the skin, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when they have become hard like leather, and are softened, if one does the same as one does to blisters:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if at such ones that are split into three angles, and at such ones that one covers like the skin of the mirtal tree, like abscesses in the angles;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if at such ones one makes a round incision, and other incisions and looks like it has been covered;
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, like a superficial abscess, you must pierce it clearly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has grown great boils, and you pierce it, if you do not extract all the boils at that time, but extract some of them.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just until the next day, then do not extract much of anything;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	make this several times from little to little, until all the boils are gone;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	The patient is of weak virtue, or a woman, or small children, or old, aged people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Those who do not have a head, like an abscess on the skin, it is necessary that you pierce it clearly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and has a great bulge, and you pierce it, if you do not draw out all of the bulge at once, but only part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing more; do this many times from one heavy to the next, until the bulge is completely gone; however, it is a weak person, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Then use this remedy with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound heals, and watch to see if the wound from the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a simple wound, then apply linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many boils, then you must tie each one with a bandage so that they come together;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have copped in the aposteme a part of leather, and you have sewed it inside, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or woolen rags dry from moisture, and tie it just until three days;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the bone, and the cure of ointment as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the pain comes to your head, then bring cold water and quickly, and wet the sheet, and put it on the place where it is hurting many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the pain of blood persists, instruct him in government and cure, and the powders that I have said to put on them in this book, and if he has fever or is wet, then you must put sheets and blankets soaked in wine and oil warm;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if he is scorched, and his limbs are swollen, it is necessary that you cover him with sheets soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until three days, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then clean out the abscess and drain it and heal it, as is right, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is what one should know universally in treating abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	For I have told you how one must proceed before treating abscesses, and now listen to me about the paste.
des soros	abces
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or treat the head of the shoulder so that small abscesses are created, and they are treated in such a way that they are like webs, as with the knee of a gown, and many have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There is grease and oil where there is moisture as well as feathers;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if it is hard and bone-like, and there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose itself.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist so that you experience all the instrument called "intramessore", from which the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if it flows from above the long way.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture has dried up, if you leave the hair that contains the moisture in place, it will stick again once it has dried up;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	and then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if there is any present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if there is none, in water and milk, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and this man who is delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And thus start the cotton again, as before, on the second day, and the third, as long as you know well that it does not stay away from night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wound with ointment to suit, as long as he is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds a lot of pus, so that the scar remains long;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and I put your scabs, and scorch all over, and put all your cure to draw the skin where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery does not go against you, do as I have said before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And so you make the abscess if it is painful, and the barber's and doctor's tools as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on the painful abscess and the wet one, for it is lighter in blood loss.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if in any of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and those that I have described, where the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess as a heavy stone, hard and pale, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if there is none, one would also have made a good wound like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses that come out at the top, it is necessary that these who come out at the tips of the ears be completely removed so that the bowel can be pushed out.
et les cure si com il covient.	and heal them as is due.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times have there been abscesses in the throat, and they drain, and cause pain, and do not go to any other place or heal, and are rotten, and one is infected with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scar is properly within its rib, like the root and the abscess at the top, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And the appearances of these scars are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that which you see of good disposition to the touch, and is the same color as the bone, and does not move from any part, nor is it deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrub each part, and the two lips of the face with one hand, if you need them, as we have said in the top abscesses.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and little by little, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve nor the vein, and do not cut it too deep, so that the hand does not escape, and do not look too far ahead, so that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	If you cover the vein or artery and it does not let you work, then put vinegar on the wound, or some powders that stop the blood, and draw the wound out.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is calm, and the wound is softened, and then begin to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood has stopped, if you return to your work, as long as you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then feel with your finger if there are any small bumps, if they are, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	If there is great pain in the root of the abscess, it only comes when you cut the abscess in its root, but leave a strong double thread and let it hang, without causing any harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then employ the wound of fine cottoncloth soaked in Egyptian ointment, then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you catch the whole plague, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound, and sewed them up, so that there is no delay from the abundance of the plague.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you hear to cover the root of it, and draw it out with force, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofula that have excess, pierce where it opens, so that it dies;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce in the same way as said before, depending on it, then I apply ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts him who is delayed from corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well washed, then heal with ointment causing confusion, until he is healed.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The old said and spoke about the scalpel of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw in our land that it was done, and this is the script of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the split of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be removed;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and let him not do it himself, for all the veins and the poison of the disease are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth or in the throat or in II adenoids.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the throat channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary then, when we want to split the epiglottis, that we do so with three circles or four small splits through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the split on the soft part, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if they are suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no chisel, and the vessel is long from one.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to its entire length, and then splits the meat as much as it comes to the wood;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then split the soft part, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the splitting of the fluid of the throat that jumps out through the place that has been broken, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed when we are in doubt about strangle, gather the two lips of the wound on both sides, and the entire cut goes under the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer drugs that cause nausea, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says: 'Do not make this cut until the throat is completely closed up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault leaves it.'
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and so the elder is commanded to leave the wound open for as long as the disease is gone, and it has passed in three days or four. And then he orders to sew up the wound and heal, until it has healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and put it in her throat, and went out into the cold.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by the healer, and I found it as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and I saw well that it had not been cut open by a vein or an artery but was coming out through the throat, and the veins were going out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed it until it was well;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and there remained with the damsel only that she was red in the face, and returned to her usual state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for on this day I would that in the cutting of the epiglottis there be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	The abscesses are called "glandular glands", and are large in size, of a yellow color, and very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	where natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is according to two manners: one seems like fat to us, and another manner seems like an abscess that comes from our blood.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and he has fear, and does not fit to act on fire furiously than in the little one who is small, and test and search all the inter-machine:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you try it too as I know, and can't do anything, if the cap, if he covers us, and treats all his coat, if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well soon, and treat it as it should be, so that it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of doing this, which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I say all the difference that exists between us and the outcome.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that the outcome is painful and feverish, as long as the bulging is passed, and the blistering is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and the heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With good health there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a fluid that is similar to the blood of the body according to its color, and it begins like a seed and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either fat or moist, and many colors are as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of our nature, you must first test and inquire about all the instruments that are called "entromissoire", according to what their shape may be or the paste that follows it.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way to extract abscesses from the body is that you squeeze or moister place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you feel the instrument has reached the bottom, then it should be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then take out the instrument, and take care not to miss anything.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs quickly, that it be of the same color as I said for the other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the instrument comes out moist, know that it is fat, so that you hold it with a pin and lightly peel it from each side and pay attention to where it lies, so that you take it out healthy with the good health.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out healthy, draw it out piece by piece so that nothing stays behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything stays behind, it returns to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if there is a little delay, and it does not trouble him, then employ some corrosive water powders to extract the wound, and put something soothing on the pustule, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it hurts us much, then count the two lips of the wound, and treat what causes the pain.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein is under a stone or another obstacle, then hurry and employ the power of vitriol, and let it rest for two or three days, until the wound is pus-filled, and pour on the blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to treat what has been delayed from the outside.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Behold the forms of the intruding instruments, and they are of three manners:
grans et moien et petit;	large and long and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and they are of three manners:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, in order to close the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles used to pierce sorcerers, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are bright yellow, and are more proven by black lead to close the abscesses of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three manners:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the aperture.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the hooks are of many appearances, as you will see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Great, medium, and small ones.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if they have two curbs of three kinds as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if they have three curbs and are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if they have two curbs, and one with only one curb, and are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these should be sharp, and some of them do not cut well but only from one side, so that we skin the nerves in order to hit the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these introverters are put back in many places so that the patient does not lose them at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and not use one more than in a good place, if legs, arms, breasts, and hands, and similar things;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never make another instrument small, resembling a scythe of beasts, according to this form, so that it does not hurt the flesh:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it on no more than once to the place that heals with a comb of veins, and arteries, and never according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	and never do men's breasts swell when they become corrupted, as much as they seem to be a woman's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and do not remain ugly and swollen, and who want to cure them, if it is appropriate according to this form of this line . b . until g .:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scalth the fat, and apply medicine to the wound washing it with water, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and cure it as long as it is healthy;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast has run down, and is soft because of its size as it would be in a woman, then make two holes on top, by two similar splits;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	of so that one is held by the other at the end of one and the other, so that the greater line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scald the skin that is between the two lips, and bone the fat, and add what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the cure, until he is well;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not well, or the incision is not yet entirely made, so that the patient does not rest, or for the escape of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it has dried up the remaining skin and fat, then treat it until it is well.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	which come from sore buttocks are managed like hard scrofula or if it has ribs, and if there is only one that contains moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	So those that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line. b. up to line. g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels that are in the abscess are empty, then plug the wound with wet cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofula, then cut it as we have said in the cutting of scrofula, and if the wound opens bowels, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin that is above it is sewn together, then many abscesses come, and also come to the escaped vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if they prick at their base, so that it is for the artery, if the abscesses are long all around.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it on both sides, if you feel extraction.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, if it is necessary to move apart gradually.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and this chapter teaches that it is foolish to cut the abscess, and least of all when it is connected to the jugular vein or to the neck and mouth of others, and it is very dangerous.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the cure of iron, and that which is at the head also must be avoided, and in that which is inflamed with an artery, it is done from above the skin with a long knife.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work on the size like a single piece of cloth, and separate the artery from the membranes very carefully until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then bottle up the blood, and let it pierce almost to the other coast, and hold back the artery with a double thread of thread in two lines according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then mark the line that is between the two knots of an introducer as far as the sun rises and sets, and let it come out, and release the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then set in motion the cure that is due to water, until the line is broken.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat with an ointment that comes from this, until he is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is near the vein, you should hold it in your hand what you can of the abscess and then bottle up the needle with moisture and let it pierce, and there are two threads, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	and tie the aposteme, if I told you, or the string of one of the two parts to the shoulder blades;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the string is not strong enough, if he returns another needle to all the thread from the first incision, and pulls out the strings in four lengths;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the aposteme until the surplus comes out, then cut the excess at the knot and leave what is tied;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on it a wet cloth in wine and oil, then bring him cures of camphor and cloves until he is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the nerves of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	So too do arteries and veins; they come from the nerves when they are hurt, or because of excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And if there are more joints, and two at a time, and in all of them or some of them, where there is a knot, it seems the same color as the blood, and it has many symptoms without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when they are restrained, if the patient feels pain, and it is not completely cured, but let it continue;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and be quiet on all sides, and do not move forward or backward, nor above nor below, and the one who is in joints does not come to cover with iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	for fear that they might contract;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are at the head or in front, make the skin with a scalp-pin.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, if it has a nail, and cut it at the root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if the suspender has an oncine, and scratch it, then break the bone and patch the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of the large bellies hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Now there comes a pain in the belly and not elsewhere, it is a disease that is called "fungus" by appearance, and its root is subtle and its head is big;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and I have both small and large ones.
