et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on top of the powder I cover with a piece of wet dried-up rosin melted with rosewater, seasoned with good oil and fresh herbs, and leave it there until the next day, and the doctor treats it with other remedies until it is well.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of treatment for this is as follows:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two shoulders should be relaxed and smooth, and the shoulders should be cut in the same way as always, evenly.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the mistake in the treatment is when the liquid escapes through the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then you must stretch it with your finger so that the veins make an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and make it even, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, hold it with pliers, and then make it even.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they exceed three days, and that which is sore in the scrotum is swollen, if he leaves it so that the abscesses are calmed, and the scorching is light.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If you cover it as well as you can, and keep away from the part near the scrotum, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	So then the powder of things that cause a sore to heal, which we have spoken of as a treatment of powders, and if you cover it too much, and it goes up, it will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So then cure, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retentlement of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to an operation on a stone, or frozen blood, or bowel, or similar things, which we have spoken of in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine does not flow freely, and you see a retention because of a stone or a knothole in the bladder, so it is necessary that the patient be lying on his knees;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and let them lie on their backs, and extend their bellies from the back side, and restrain the patient so that they remain as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then constrict the colon of the bladder to the excretion of stone above, so that the urine is discharged and;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must bring in the instrument that is called a syringe, from which there is this form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and be of fine lightweight silver, as the feathers of an owl;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and be of the length of a palm and a half, and be flexible at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the discharge of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it to the tip with a piece of wool or cotton, and dip the tip into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the superfluity of the lamp and pour it up to the head of the syringe, then oil the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and inflate the bladder and foreskin with moist oil and olive oil and water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then insert the syringe lightly into the foreskin up to the root of the foreskin, then turn the foreskin over towards the bladder;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then fill the syringe up to just before the bladder, and let the patient go until it comes to the hollow thing, and if it is not done according to this order then it will turn around and go back;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then draw the thread through all the wool, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and let the urine run;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and begin the syringing as long as the bladder is empty, and equalize the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or sores come to the bladder, and it is swollen, and you see there distilling water and medicines, so do for all the instrument which is called "clepsydre", and that is like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has three openings:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	On one side, and on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the hair cut so that the medicine goes in such a way that it stops well the prick without addition, if one can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see to move your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the catheter in the moisture, and push while moving which is above;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	you will draw out the moisture to the catheter, and then push hard the catheter above;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture enters, it will come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder:
si est ci:	If so:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or of archchant, and this head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and the chin or the jawline;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a lamb's bladder and put the moisture that you have distended the bladder, then place it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the moisture over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then pour the distended bladder into the scrotum, then draw your hand over the bladder taking out all the moisture in turn, so that the patient feels that the moisture has been drawn into the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle on it, and pierce it roundly;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then pour in a strong thread into these perforations, then join the circle together as you would join a seam, and put inside it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do so as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already spoken about the division of stones and their extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I have said about the difference between a stone in the kidney and all the signs, and that a stone must be operated on by cutting;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone that is lodged in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and it is a sign that the fluid jumps from the bladder into the thin substance next to it like water in its thinness;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and I hold him back, and massage his penis, and I bend it many times, and then I rub it;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and at the end of these movements, the basis is broken;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and is lighter the healing of children until they are four years old, and is bitter in elders, and is like the moaning of those who are between juvenile and elderly.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and is lighter the cure of those who have a large stone, than that of those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary first to purify the patient with enemas, in order to remove all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never bothers to seek a stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and move him up and down, so that the stone comes out to the perfection of the bladder, and do not cut it from the top;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make him sit between your hands, and his legs are drawn up, so that the bladder hangs down;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then look into it and touch it;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in space, then hurry to cut off the stone above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not chide when you touch all of it, then wet your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the disease is difficult, or your middle finger, if the disease is in its infancy.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and put it on its foundation, and feel the stone, and when you feel it in your two hands, if the pain is at the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press toward your two hands, and the bottle away from where you see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the minister to press the bladder in his hand, and he commands that he extends the testes in his right hand above, and with his left hand hold the skin that is soothed by the testes on the part where one cuts.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then pour the semen, for this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And open between what is between the testes and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be right on the stone, and your two hands be next to the foundation, and be the cut deep as the quantity of the stone allows, not too big;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by chance, the press if it must be who is or foundation, so that it jump out without work;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and knows that there is a piece of stone or angle, and margins:
si est griés a issir;	if it grinds to issue;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is a piece of wood that seems like a nut, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	a cell then where it has angles and margins, make the incision larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not grind, then you extract it on the claws that are like a file at the head, so that the stone does not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you put on it an instrument of silver finely ground on the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot fix it like this, then open it with a sharp edge, and if it bleeds, then extract it with vinegar;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, then bottle the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then push it out forcefully, and the smaller ones after if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If the stone is large, then it is necessary to make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things come to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	where he dies, or his urine comes again quickly because the leg cannot hold it.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	however, you must try to pull it out with pliers, or cut it off with knives, as long as you pull it out in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have finished your work, if you apply the wound with oil and wine, or with oil and cold water and rosewater to calm the inflammation;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then remove the patient's bladder, and do not separate the ligature until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, so that it returns to its place well with oil and water, then cure it with unguent of honey and unguent of basil until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if abscesses come into the wound and putrefaction, and freezing of blood in the bladder, and is retained by this that the urine goes up, which is congealed in some way so that it does not go down with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Now therefore you must put on poultices in the wound, and extract this blood, because if it remains, it corrupts the bladder and makes it pus:
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then raise the wound with water and earth and straw, and help him in all ways that you can until he is healed;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that every day that you cure him, you bind his two legs and put the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	If the stone is small, and it is in the bladder, and it is pushed out, and the urine cannot come out:
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the cure for what I have said above, that you cut it many times, is a reason for this cure to be excused from cutting:
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proved this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron and forge it according to this form, and let it be III angles nailed in one piece of wood:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	and take a piece of leather and fasten it to the root of the penis so that it cannot move backwards towards the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then pour the liquor into the penis lightly until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and return the awl to your hand in the stone little by little, so that you can pierce the stone from another side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	so that urine will soon flow out, then press your hand on him who is delayed from the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it has been broken and gone flying with the urine, and the patient has relieved himself, he is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot achieve this by any means so that it is damaged, then take a piece of leather and fasten it to the stone and another above it, then pull it out forcefully, and after removing the leather, clean the frozen blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the healer as long as he remains healthy.
de la piere des femmes	from the woman's bone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	There is a chance that it will occur in women, and if it does not happen once, there is a great harm to the healer, and is defended by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	the first is that per adventure the woman is virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-informed who reveals herself to spooks, even if she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third way is that per adventure one cannot find a woman well-informed in this craft of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth way is that the woman's hand is more perfect than the man's hand, so that it covers it better and causes greater pain. And if necessity demands it, you should take a female healer who is well-informed, and not a male healer, for if you do not find one, there is no point in seeking one.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and the present a skilled dancer in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands that she do what you command of the extraction of stones;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and watch very well whether the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is convenient to put his finger or foundation and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she pricks it, so that the finger is released from her grasp, and he recommends that she puts her finger or thumb in the malady, and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder in form.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she pricks it, so that she moves it with great force from the entry of the bladder to the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut into the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle part, where it is moved, and feel the stone in that part;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his two above the stone or cut off, and let it size the first small;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then bottle up pour on the waist, if you feel the stone so large the wound as the stone can come out again, and know that there are many ways of stones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	it is to say, small and large, sharp and rough, long and round, and which have rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearances so as to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if it does not go out, put on the vitriol burn, and keep it for an hour as long as the wound is not cured;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have tools that I have told you in the extraction of the stone from men to help you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if it does not go out, and this is the artery that is cut off, put the powder on the spot and strain it from thick and thin, and do not recommence it, and leave the stone and do not extract it, except by accident the patient dies;
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the fire has subsided, and the blood has stopped flowing, if you return to your work, let the stone be far away.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnous
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	water is nothing but a collection of white or clear blood, which causes the dislocation of the joints, which contains the egg.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and is called "syfac", and never properly in the yolk of the egg, if one believes that it is another egg.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	is the skin of the joint between the white or clear blood that we have mentioned;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and if it does not come to nothing.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is so feeble that it comes from the utters, and that material is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never by impact on the joints, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	where it is a color that changes to yellow, or is without red, or black, or white water, and this happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of this collection, for if it is white or clear blood as we have said, then there is pain in the abscess, and a long poke as in an egg, and does not close the joints, because it has moisture all around it.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the own towel, then is the aposteme reason with a part of the egg, and because of this one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if there is moisture between the leather of the testicles and the white silk, then does he feel bad;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you want to know the color of the moisture, try it on all the intimate parts as much as possible so that its shape is in front.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the shell, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we heal him with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his power and the repletion of his body;

puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit down on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the stick to one of the 12 ribs on the side of the testicles;

cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	and peel all or by pieces separately the skin of him subtilely, that if you do not peel it well bleeding, so will return the water;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the wind blows to your work, so you reset in its place when you have completed the work of the Syphac;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then join the two limbs at the knee joints with one seam, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the hock corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you hang the feet that are suspended, in doubt of the decay of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cut off the leg at the suspension, and extract the hock, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the hock is assembled in two parts together, know that they are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	then cut off the other part as you did the first one, making it even, then wash the blood, and put in the wound another moist thing made of oil rosin;

et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two shoulders on the two arms, and let all of it be assembled in the loop of the breeches;

et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is safer.
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and keep the blood from flowing out, and be careful about the work of cutting.

Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not wait for this work because of its horror, then make a perforation, as I have said to you, and it is that when you are sure by the signs which we have said that the water is hot, then place the patient on a raised seat;

et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the towel does not let the water run out of the wound's mouth, then you must put in a tube or the instrument with which one draws off the water from the hydropses, so that it forms as before;

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the severing of this limb there are many dispositions, so that I think it is better to leave it;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you about the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I therefore say that many abscesses come from the cors, and most importantly the injections.
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is because of moisture.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say, by acrid and sour water that spreads into the injections, or by impact;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the cors.
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And does not indicate pain, and is an abscess of sadness;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there are some abscesses that are painful and piercing, and of a purple color, and never come from an artery, or swelling in the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, if you know by the position of the abscess that it is hot, then when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and only touch it slightly.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	What is done by swelling in the vein is known by its expression when touching with the fingers, and one can make the size of this appearance, and of the other characters;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and so you take care of the curings of the joints, then place the egg on top, and the trail further down from the white milk, and free the suspender from all sides of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already soaked with these new oils, then it is necessary that you then draw out the egg and the coating.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is white within, or in what is inside the containers, then you must free all of it, and the coating rolls around.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the horse is from behind, then you should cut it all, and remove the membrane, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then employ the wound with wet wool in oil and wine, and then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess surrounded by a wrapping that resembles a barnacle, with the softening of the joints, and the patient groans greatly when it moves.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this disease is very similar to that which we have described above, and we will tell you the way to do it according to what the old man did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	He should have you sit the patient on one side of the bed with his legs raised, then pour the potion of suspension between his thighs, all along the vessel that is near the penis, and spread it well on the skin.

puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut them in the middle, correctly according to the length of the body, and thus extract the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound as with others where a bow has been shot, so that no vessel churns and makes one of the testicles rot.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	Car by God it comes not of evil, and so all vessels come forth, if is necessary to draw the semen from all vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	So that the oven does not lose its freshness because of the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	about the surgery of the sick
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The movements of this rat come about because of the incision that comes out or extends on the belly in the part of the anus, so that the intestines descend from that cut to one of the chambers;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	And this cut is where the pain comes from or because of the extension of it, and these two ways come about because of moisture from these two causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	Or because of impact, or leap, or braying, or lifting a burden, and by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is an extension of pain, if it comes slowly and slowly, for a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the aposteme is even until almost at the end, so that the medicine hastens the intestine.

And the signs are when it is a section of syphilis that sudden pain comes, and the apostemes are different appearances, dislodging the skin; and this is due to the exit of the intestine and the body away from syphilis.

de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnous
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this recipe I have never seen anyone dare to try to make the cure with fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old people said that it is done in this way as the vine that ties the vine, so that you tie the branches, after the size of a little bit on the leg;

de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the crotch
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Often the leather of the testicles is softened in some men, so that the spermatozoa inside are softened, and it can be seen;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	And it is necessary, when you treat him, to make the man lie down, and to pull off the skin which is softened on top of the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	Then join the two lips with one stitch, and you will see, cut first the excess of the softened skin at three stitches or four firmly;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Then pull between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and let it ooze.
dou chastrement	Dou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	For if I were to say this, then it would be against our custom.
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is not necessary for just two ways:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	where one is that the mirror should answer when asked, and in a mirror's cure;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, for if we have often had a need to chastise certain animals to help us, as with rams and sheep and hogs and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say then that chastisement is done in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	where by attraction or by splitting apart.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In that which we do with attraction, let us sit the animal in hot water until its testicles are softened and while they are still soft;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then grab them with your hand, until they have healed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the lancing of wounds:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	You must take the best cow, and bring its hide to your left hand, then tie it up with the strap, and cut off each hoof when you have well skinned them.
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and I leave no hole of syrup or sugar which is over the veal;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this way of lancing is to be preferred over that which is done by attraction, for in the latter case there may be something about the hooves that causes the cow to crave luxuriance;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then heal the wound as long as it is well.
des hermofrodites	Of the chastisement of size: It is fitting that you anoint the bestial, and press the skin of the hoglets to your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cover each hoglet with I know not how many; leave no small poultice of the si-fac and sub-tifat which is on the vasselins; and this mode of chastisement is mature that which is done by attraction, for thisu that to the attraction remains by adventure nothing of the hoglets, by coi the bestial desires luxure; then heal the wound as long as it is healthy.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphrodite is according to two manners as men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	the one if it is that between the two hooves as it is made by nature of a woman, or it have hair, and sometimes the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has on the breast as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the healing of man and woman is that you cut off the hoofs together, and heal them as other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second way, men whose urine jumps out of their loins, unless they are cured.
de la tentigene	of the tentacle
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	The tail is tied to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	And some women have also great wonder at it, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you take the surplus of the tail to your hand or fingers, and make a small cut;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not cut too deep, that the blood does not flow much, then heal with another cure as long as it is healthy;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and at another tail that is born in the mouth of the mare, and use it, and perhaps it will jump out, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this they called it the old "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you need to cut it, as we have said about the tongue, and treat it until it is healthy.
de erratique	of irregular
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the hernia is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	And is natural by birth, or happens through disease that came to it;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	Or is made by the art of the jester, or by the subtle or specific medicine, and is made perfect in the mare, or in the coast, or dissection, or what not;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and can be conceived, and birth, and by chance flowers to have;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this is through the way of the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	For if the stoop is close and apparent, whether it is at your two sides or above.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is subtle medicine, and it is near to leaves, if you hurry, and around thus:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	meet your two fingers together, and the woman be on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then are the two fingers formed, until the subtle medicine is running, and the support is removed;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take wool, and wet it in oil, and put it on the place, and let the woman lie with each man every day, so that he cannot hold it together.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the remedy is harsh and thick, then it is necessary that you take a kind of spa water resembling a mint leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If he is stuck in a car, if he is suspended by the neck and the cloak.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and put medicines that stop the blood, if necessary, blood of dragon, incense, together with a lot of incense;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then provide a long, wide piece of cloth, so that the wound cannot heal;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and let it hang for a long time, and bring a tent made of dry linen;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with other treatments until he is well.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	When the woman is pregnant, and you cover her according to this method, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the case of an abscess that is in the womb, one must not touch fire.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that require no surgery, and when hemorrhoids are old they become throbbing;
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the signs of disease, and the symptoms, and I will say here those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thump are perfect in the marriage, and they do not appear in feeling unless it is cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the vagina can be felt, and those who can be cured are cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, and tie her to the bed, and cover her with clothes, and powder her with medicines that stop the blood, if necessary, blood of dragon, incense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	Then put his feet on the wall for an hour, then place them in cold water.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if the wound comes, so that the fat is poured out, then place it in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and thus, and apply it to his back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If this does not work, then place air cushions on his back and massage without hurting;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take another one, and squeeze it to extract the juice of plantain or of gorse with old wine, and apply it to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess has healed, then treat the wound until it is well;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "spelt" is red, and is like to I sharp chief, so cover it as I have said in the recipe;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat him as long as he is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	the abscesses of the married woman
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Various kinds of abscesses come in the married woman, such as plaguey and piercing abscess, herpes and estias and fistula and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	Therefore, it is necessary that in this treatise, the apothecary's cautery which comes to the femur, which is not a constant abscess but a burning one;
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you know the work of fire, see if the abscesses are tender at the beginning of their appearance, and if they are hot and feverish, and if they turn red, then you can see them.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore, do not hurry to pierce it, but let him die as long as the pain is not relieved;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit down on two small seats, so that he leans his back and joins his legs away from the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and may their hips be spread out, and place their arms behind their knees, and tie them well with a good bond;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	Then suck the bile down towards the left coast, and I will prepare the instrument with which one works the mouth of the womb, from which comes this form thereafter.
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you see me prepare this instrument, that you put the point first in to test the depth of the womb so that what enters through the instrument comes out perfectly as it should and does not hurt the patient.
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the womb with cloth so that the instrument does not hurt it.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he put the tip of the instrument on top and dip the instrument into water.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess opens and you hold it with your hand, if it is necessary to cover the apex, the most painful part;
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the bow is empty, if it is necessary that you put in the wound wet rags soaked in oil of roses, or dry green oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the poultice perfectly over the wound and peste on the wound and on the other hand clean rags wet with water or fried seeds;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the healer after two days of poulticing coming to this, as long as it is healthy;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and never raise the poultice and the wound by the use of water and honey, and then by water or long roots of lys and arislage are cooked;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then recover to poulticing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healing in the scar, you must keep yourself from cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	The first thing is for the woman who gives birth to know the signs of nature, and if you see her press down, and she desires to smell the air:
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	Then let the fire cautery be applied.
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	And now I will tell you that these children are according to their natural figures, and this one comes out with its head, and the second with it.
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, if you lightly press his belly, then that child will come soon;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when it descends on its head, then the second with him, and thus cleanses the marriage of its excesses by good purification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this one that comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes in no way on its feet, but comes on the chest or shoulder, and the hands, or comes on the belly, or sometimes, and is turned around by accident on the neck, and by other bad shapes;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	so that you may dance wisely and cunningly in these things, and be warned of error and deception; and I will show you all the shapes how to help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If she falls forward by her own natural force, and the woman gives birth in pain, and her virtue is weak, so that it fails when she sits on a saddle or when women hold it.
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and pour over her with oil or fennel seed that has been cooked, and then pour the balm between her two little spatulums whose form is described here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and split the second one, and cut off his fingernail until the moisture that causes it to crack comes out.
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press on the woman's belly until the fetus moves, and if it does not move, then it is necessary to apply musk oil made from fenugreek with sesame oil;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make her press and shake off the condensing, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	so that she may now deliver the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands are hot, then you must repeat the process of gently squeezing them a little and a little:
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a chair and lift her feet up.
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then remove the chair from under the woman, and tie her down so she doesn't stand up;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if his hands cannot enter, and the baby dies, then cut the hands off with the knife that is placed in front, and pull out the baby, and cut it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	in the delivery of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes on its feet, if you put a stick up;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it back and forth until it is even;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	and then stretch it out and bend it back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Until he jumps just as high as his knees, if you command him to jump, and make him shake with fear;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he jumps, may God help him.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not turn out as we have said, then let it be turned little by little, until it is back in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For now it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if he does not come as we have said, then take musk of alyssum, and oil of sament, and gum melted, and grind it all together in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put on her nature within and without this ointment, then make her sit in warm water until she is soaked to the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is wet all over, she is given a chain of myrrh, and it is put on her, and she is left for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a seat, then make her shake and hold her mouth and nose, and press her belly lightly, for the child is coming now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child between his legs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the baby comes in this form, if I put my hand on his head little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then be bound around his neck, and hang his feet down, and lie down on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend his hands little by little, and then press his hands on his belly, and pull out the bowels all at once, until she is emptied;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if it does not jump, then take its feet and move its body, then move its body above its belly, then put your hands on it.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and strike the child little by little;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and command the woman to lean back as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	When the child is born with one hand extended,
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to learn how to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then let the woman get up and go.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then let her lie down on the bed, and make her stretch her legs straight;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then arrange the muscles as I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then let her sit on a chair, and study to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and form the child according to its natural shape, and make it shake, and command the woman to lean back as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the baby's delivery through its mother's groin, and it spread its hands, and its face turned towards her back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the barber shave his hand, then turn it a little at a time, and wipe it lightly.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, if he puts the musk that we have mentioned on top of it, and oil, then he orders her to move a little at a time;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, if you place it on a seat, and he orders her to lie down;
et la fai esternuer.	and make her shake.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same method for all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When he comes in this way for the whole second time, if you cover your nail with it until the moisture is empty;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if he puts it on his face and neck, and covers it up so that it cannot be held back, then the barber dies;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, until you have put it in as it should be, and order the woman to lie down once:
adonques si istra legierement.	So then it is lightened a little.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the twin's issue
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	It is known that good things come often, and never more than three or four at a time;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	And this is not an unusual thing, and it rarely happens;
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are an unusual thing, and they never live, if only one were left;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that, if they are multiplied, they are lost by the fire which devises them, which is tied to the lead;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And never are they born naturally as all of us, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	If they are born with pain, if the cure is as we have said, and let the wise doctor do it quickly and lightly;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and then do it so that it may be saved.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	And never is it formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more than fifteen, and all are formed by the measurement of the wise glorious, and know the doctor everything, for by chance similar things might be there;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Do as you see fit.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman who has given birth to a dead child or is pregnant and it does not come out, and you are forced to use your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	if the woman is of sound health, and there is no accident that she might fear death from;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	if the woman is pinned beneath her back and her hips are tilted downward, and her legs are raised up;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife ties the cords from both sides, so that she is tied to the bed, so as not to be treated for the delivery of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oil mixed with ale and fenugreek seed and flaxseed, then ointment her hands with this oil and these muskellion seeds;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	Then pour into the woman's body lightly, and then see if the child is ready to be born, and take care that the baby is dressed properly so that it does not come out in pieces;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	If he inserts the hairpins into his hair or into his neck or into his mouth or onto his cheek or onto his chin or near his sides, and the pins are inserted or pricked through the skin, then they must be cut off at the base and the blood should flow.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	And he should hold the hairpin in his right hand and place the thumb of his left hand between the two fingers of his right hand, and grip it lightly with his entire hand, and insert the hairpin into any one of these places that we have described until he reaches the empty space.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	This is the form of the hairpin:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	Then take another hairpin and place it in such a way that the pricks are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	And then stretch it evenly from one side to the other, so that it stands up, and fix the hairpins with their points in such a way that they cannot move, as follows:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if some part of it remains, if he oil one of his two ends and bottles it up in that part, and draws the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there is no delay at all, he places this ointment or more high and does it until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back due to the tightness, then you must wrap it in a sheet until it comes out completely;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	Then take it in the joint of the sole or at the neck, and in this way you must do with the other hand, and with the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's shoulder is large and stuck in the exit, or has an acute joint assembled, then you must bottle the thorny sputum between your two joints, and cut off the joint and extract the thorn.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	where you have the instrument which is called "almahide", from which the form comes with the tools or paste which follows this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and so also it makes the natural man sick.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then draw out the bones with nails, and the head of the shoulder is forced, so that it is cut, as much moisture comes out as possible.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then chop it into pieces so that you can take it out.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or burst the ribs, so that it is necessary for you to pierce it as much as the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if he falls on his feet, then is the light आकर्षण, and the treatment is at the mouth of the wound.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stuck in the belly or in the foot, so that you can take it out with the cloth wrapped around your hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and cut open the belly or the foot, as much moisture as comes out.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other limb is ossified and the shoulder remains in place, then pull the hand completely out of the socket and draw it up to the mouth of the socket.
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then pour some wine or water onto one or two, and draw it forward.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the socket is constricted by an abscess that has come up, and it cannot work, then you must use moist and greasy substances;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and prepare poultices, and cut them into sharp, moistening, and soothing materials.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the hernia is on his rib cage, and you can make it flat, then prepare what we have said for the live child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if you do not have the ability, then draw it forward piece by piece and leave nothing of the second.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, prepare what we have said for short, sharp wounds that come in through the socket;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if the blood flow comes from the wound, then it is put in water restraining, and other treatments are given.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had been killed, then consult another on that one, and kill the others.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, the twenty feet came out of the boat, and they began to grow large.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, and I could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong plaster, and after a few days more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled much, for this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I want to stop the bleeding, and with my hands as soon as the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and waited for the woman long time then, and it was fixed a little bow from its place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not remembered this paste before that for one who, when the master tries an strange thing, he knows how to put help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the wife back to her bed
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Here comes the form of the pressure, where we place the books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and on two sides are two shoulders.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns are thinner than the restringent, and it is made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the tube should be as wide as a palm, and the margin of the tree should be, and one palm and a half long;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and the two limbs are fixed by this means, which are bent in one and in the other, half a palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two joins are inserted into the mouth of the jaw to open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, its appearance being more subtle and lighter, is made of oak or boxwood, according to the appearance of the nails;
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and has two joins, as you see, a palm long and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you see the jaw opened by all the instrument, so place the woman on the bed, her feet hanging and her legs open, then join the two joins together in the jaw, and hold the head of the instrument between her knees;
