puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then join your hand to all the instrument, as you did with the nails equally, according to the quantity that you saw the mouth of the jaw open, until the ball moves in place;
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	The instruments are all mounted upside down, and multiplied for their appearances.
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	And when you have set up the mirrors, so much faster is the operation, and higher are the men for their number.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If I do not despair of the instrument, you have not prepared it well, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second is ready for birth, it is necessary that you instruct the woman to keep her hair in place, and then make her sneeze, and hold your hands away from her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she does not, well is it.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If she does not, I can take a piece of wood or a lid and put herbs that can open the mouth of the woman, like thyme, Rue, Anise, Chamomile, Cassia, and Cento;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or none of them, are boiled or poured in water over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a lid or a pot on it, and another one in her mouth, and make her swallow as the vapors come inside her;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	Then make it shake, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If a person has had surgery.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	If it remains after this treatment and is not well, order the patient to soak his left hand in oil of sesame or in musk of ale, and then put it back in its place, and then wants the second.
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when he has found it, if he pulls it and stretches it little by little correctly, so that the bones do not ache at extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but then move it lightly from side to side, and then stretch it;
si venra et se desaerdra.	then come and dislodge it.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the patient's mouth is closed due to extraction, we have said the treatment of shaking and fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it does not improve from all that we have said, then be careful not to fool around when you stretch it;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the mare, you bind him to the loins of the woman, and then cauterize with ointment tetrafarmaçon;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if she will become pregnant and continue, and it will come strongly;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but then, when it comes to a bad smell in the stomach and head of the patient, and blisters the sick person.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	So then are fitting fوميجations suitable for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	no one of the elders has tried smoke with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument to which you will add the smoke of the flowers and the second one if this is it:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And is it like to a dog, and put the head subtly in nature, and the shoulders wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the smoke be on the coals, and the tan as long as it is spent, and restart another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet had the fundament pierced, but they are softened by a subtle and safe poultice:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	If it is necessary for him to touch the medicine to his palm, and he does not touch it with his index finger, and he holds back the string that binds it so it doesn't touch;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dip in another moist liquid, made of wine and oil, and then the cure of ointment until he is well.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not recover, put a splint on the leg, and let it hang by the hand, and be careful when it walks upstairs.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And never does the cautery come from sudden inflammation of a wound or abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	If it is necessary to cover the sudden inflammation:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	then treat, as we have said, with the poultice of vinegar.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula at the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistula that comes from the fundament is nodation, and it hurts more than those that come from the fundament defuer, or in the space between the two parts, if to one fistula or more;
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that nodation is old, if it is opened, and then wet with a warm white or yellow poultice, and never are these fistula persistent;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and are caused by that which he has or wind or fever when the sick makes an effusion, and by chance in jumping one down.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there is a fistula that pierces just up to the bladder, and just up to half of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and arrive just up to the junction of the thigh, and just up to the notch at the top of the chest.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus it is known if the fistula pierces down to the roots, and not if it pierces down:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and is when you blow on your little finger or root, and blow a fine needle of gold or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has a curve, and you blow a little piece of thread or hair from a horse as far as your finger can feel it:
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you don't feel it, and there is neither an effusion nor a fever nor wind; as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	that it does not pierce
si te haste dou curer.	if you hurry to heal
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches just to the bladder or just to the urinary conduit, if then the urine jumps out, and cannot be held back by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced just up to the join of the thigh, if so be coming up just to the edge;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twist and the pain between the bones, if so be he has already bowing back, and does not want for medicine or suddenly by touch;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent sores there is no cure except work, and the vain vanity of foolish people who mix themselves up with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In that which is not persistent and not old, there is hope for health by fire, if so be as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lets his legs go up to his thighs, and his thighs bend towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then pour out a little water, or a little mud if there is twist, until you know where the pain comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels pain in the fundament, then it is necessary that you insert your index finger there, and you will feel that the tendon is pinched.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and see whether between your thumb and the wrist or between your index finger and the wrist there is pain, so you know that it is persistent.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not bother you, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	By stretching it, one can perhaps heal some of them well, but this is little done;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that can be given is that if one heats the subtle cauldron according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and pour into it hot along the fistula, until it comes out from the fundament;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and make this two or three times, until you know that the scar tissue has been burned, which resembles a bird's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the doctor of tent-cloth immerses, until it has dried, and then the doctor of ointment rubs and dries.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is healthy, then that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	For if not, there is no cure for him;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if he tenters between them and does not pierce until the back which is at the base, and between the two tents there is an thick covering of tar or syrup, and you see the fistula to that who comes out from under the covering with a cure;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if the patch of the beginning of the fistula, and bottles immediately before the tent, and then the cure after, until it comes to the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tent will be delivered, and he will be cured;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then the tar-cloth which is made like a feather seems, and there remains nothing of it.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood does not come out, and you cut between yourself and the work, then cauterize with fire or with bitter medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cure brings together two things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	This is to know, the burning of these saddles, and the cooling of blood and the drying of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure of wet tents dries or in a house cooked, until it gets hot, and those who have been burned are put into these saddles in the fire.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound of burning tar melting hard wood, and are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it has been reset, if it has healed properly and does not come out again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the very foundation of the body and is separated from the chest, then it should be cut off at the root, and such things should be dug out.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and within it is the cloth or the tar or the saddles, or it is ready to pierce, if there is not only a way of hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you chop it just to the bone, or if you can put wet tents and cure it as first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not chop too much in perfection that you cover the foundation which holds the ground, and come the excrements by the voluntary sense;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	and the doctor, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	If he should recover, then take off that covering and clean it thoroughly from the base, or with a cloth or some other instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	and burn up that wood which is in the wound, as well as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	and study to restore the wound and keep the fistula open at the base:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	for it is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And never let the fistulas be made in this way:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and when you pierce a tent into the fistula, and it is or is attached to the base of the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I pour in water into it in two, and plug the tent into all the thread in the fistula as long as it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is piercing into the margin of the base from within, then pull out the thread of that pierced one, so that you pierce your finger or hand at the base:
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and train the head of wool, and join together the two shoulders, and hold one to the other, and leave it for a day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and do not restrain it once, until the wool has covered these joints that are between two, and have chafed;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound as long as it is souded and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if he is not too deeply imbedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not fit to make a cover with a perfect seam, and then heal, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spine with thorns that one makes a fistula if it is moistened with one, part and cut.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand not, so that we do not cover what we should not cover, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	The amputations are according to two manners:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	where they are inside the foundation, as a grain of resin, and have small and large ones, and cut short there, one or more, and are removed from the foundation and from the head of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are far away, if there is a little moisture, and again soon or a little yellow water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those who have them deep in the foundation, so that you command the patient that he should sweat himself in the chambers as long as the foundations come out, and the children are born;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry and cut it like claws, or if you hold it with your nail, then chop it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and the ligature cannot keep them in place because of their moisture, take them with a towel, or cotton, or a piece of calico;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them with your two hands, then chop them and powder them with any hot powders that are available as a cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterizing paste, for other cures until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if its foundation cannot be removed, then cauterize the patient with a hot blade and harshness so that it can wash what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	And if the patient is bleeding, and his vein is near the surface, then the cure is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And you shall hold them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them off, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and do not make an incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If it is necessary to bring the wound together in this way:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pass the thread over the top of the needle and pierce it from the other side, then return the two ends of the thread through the eye of the needle, and so it is wide;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and draw out the thread forming it, then tie the thread, and draw out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave it there for to take away the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation with a wet cloth or oil rosin, and put on the foundation, and instruct the patient that he rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until it bleeds, and when they stop bleeding, if they are treated with ointment and other treatments until they are healed;
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	to dry at the end or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying out in the intestines, and by necessity of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is no good.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary that you hold the edge of a scalpel or your fingernail above it, which does not allow it to dry out;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	and then treat it until it is hard as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot harden, if you begin to shave it more forcefully than before, until it bleeds again, and is scorched;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat him until he is well.
dou fremit	Do not sweat.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Flesh is a small thing that grows over the body, and it covers everything perfectly.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and there is no time when the wound does not ache, and one can feel it everywhere as if one were dead, and it goes all over the body, and more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the healer should take a feather from an goose, or a strong vulture's feather, and put that feather on the wound, until the purple circle surrounds the entire wound;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around all of the feather as you hold it all around the wound, and make it perfect, and clean the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so make this of a dog's head or iron according to this form, and be subtle and run on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	do not pierce it, so that it does not fall apart, and it must be pressed.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, cauterize the wound, as it is in front of or with fire of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cautery
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	No silver clistere, or archaut, or melted arain, or metal;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and no small or large instruments are made from them according to the disease that they are used for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	This is used therefore in the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cautery small and great is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and I have seen a swelling or the belly is tied up, as you see it, and the navel is pierced inside;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and one of the ribs has a hole, and the other;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly or a cow's bladder or parchment is put into one, and all small holes are pierced with a thin thread between each hole, then a strong knot is tied around the belly like a sheepskin, then it is sewn together;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, if the instrument lies in front of a strong thread, then cauterize;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or ambergris or some other thing, then pour it lightly;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the ministers hold it with both hands until it is completely dry, then remove the cloth, and place the patient's legs against the wall, and let the medicine flow out, as much as it can;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night, that is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize him with fire because of a disorder of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then wait until he is well again.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, then let the cloth also be very thin like for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the shape of the thin cloth over the skin so that it is held back:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicament, selonc l'acomplement.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are, and according to the places where they are made, and according to how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicament, selonc l'acomplissement. Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicament, selonc l'acompliment. Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicament, selonc l'acompliment. Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblan
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when there is a simple wound where the bone is not broken, but take care for it may be from a stone or similar thing, and the skin is all torn and the wound is large, and you doubt about the temp of an abscess.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if the pain comes to the head so quickly after the wound, and is opposite to where the wound was made;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and denies himself wine and meat that is fattening.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not improve, if his flesh is growing less, and he does not drink wine or eat cheese;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put a hot cloth on the wound, if an abscess forms, wet it only with oil and then wrap it up, or with wine that is stinging.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no temp in it, if it lies still on the wound, not moved by air or powder, which I will speak of a little further on;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if he has been burned, then put it on some ointments until he is well.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, as from a sword or similar weapon, and the lips cannot be joined by stretching, but must be joined with sutures, just as I say about abdominal wounds, from the stitch.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open and raw, and bleeding, and only holds but to a pok, then bind it up.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then treat the wound with medicine, and return to using hard food instead of soft leather, and instruct the patient to eat hearty meats, such as roasted meat and eggs, as well as poultry and other similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find leather putrefaction, and it does not touch the bone, then bind it firmly, and pour on it a strong solution, and then treat it;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if he has an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped with medicine, then seek the artery, and if you find it displaced, then mend it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not help, then apply fire to cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light.
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and that you put this powder in so that the fire will move it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is thus:
pren encens une partie;	take incense a part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	Dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	burn the incense part, dragon's blood three parts, and the powder, and apply it to the wound, and tie it up tightly, until it heals well and joins together all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then he bandages it well, and leaves it undissolved, if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for the medicine should not be applied until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never does one use only live charm when incense or dragon's blood has moved the wound; but that fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has moved the wound, even slightly, then there is no need to apply this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put upon some garlic that has been infused, or grain of wheat made with water and honey, until it heals.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then the doctor prescribes other treatments as long as he is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break in the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with careful pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the breaks in the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound at the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is at the throat and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the artery at the throat is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a newborn, if there is no other device than to let the cure take place, and do not put anything restraining, because it harms the newborns and makes them retreat;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, because the substance of the newborns is cold, and their growth continues with the brain, which is the highest limb;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be hot, as warm water, and mixed with rosewater oil, and let it also be washed with fresh water, and other stones of the mines according to this way, and moistened with moisternails;
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with bends, and then treat until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and she is full of bowels, then pierce her or lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes from it, so she loses consciousness, and her pulse stops, and she is cauterized, then the profession of surgery must be done;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the larynx is cut, or the windpipe, and it is blocked up so that the meat goes down, then cut the windpipe at the base of the larynx, and do not touch the larynx but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then let it rest for some days, and then treat it with garlic until it is cured;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has impressed the bone, then cut it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, then cut them all off so that you cannot have it, and leave the wound to rot and putrid, and let the pus come out;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I said in my chapter on the ointment.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a cut from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then look up at the patient's face:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	then know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and the wound is fresh to its very heart, then do not put on the powder yet, nor bind it up so that it does not heal completely, and return to the body, and let the patient rest;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I will put on a healing ointment, and bind it up twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have ointment, put raw wool in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more often;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	If I do not come to spasm, or a bad tremor from the heart or any strange extraction of bone;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see these good conditions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the wounds with ointment and other remedies as long as he is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	And if it cannot be healed, and operates, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the healing is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision with a knife or a spear, and it is simple, or deeper or on the back, then know the cure of this one who is ahead;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, from sewing;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, from powder, and if it has entered the bone, and has broken it into pieces, then examine the wound, and the difficult cuts if they are dislocated;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not removed, then let the wound fester, and let the extractions be equal.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds or other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Dou derrompement du ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the abdomen is great and painful and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a large wound, sometimes the intestines break out or separate from one another, so that the entrails are broken up;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suture is more difficult, and there is no reason to put any less effort into a small wound than a large one, for if we do not sew them together inch by inch, the intestines will separate.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	so that the intestines swell up so that they feel cold, then put them back in place again, and for a small wound, because we leave it longer than the other wounds,
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	and know that the rupture of the abdomen has four ways to happen:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common stitches are in the stitch of the womb, and the stitch of the other wounds of the chest and two other proper stitches are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and each of them is more appropriate with the stitch of the womb, and I will say one by one and I will declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and there is nothing of the intestine out, and there is no need to mend it, this is done in one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or for the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, heat it in one of these two ways:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or II dry cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook it in lukewarm water and fenugreek and cumin and spices, and rinse the intestine until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never does this wine causing constriction, and it is bitter to the soul for expelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling subside, if you moisten the intestine with water or alcohol and cook the herbs, because by this is restricted the entrance to a small thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a little hole in the wound with the instrument with which one cuts the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to cut off what needs to be cut off, and we do not want to cut it unless there is a great need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it cuts from within towards the core and not away, and thus consider this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are protruding, if you can put it back in its natural place in its own proper place, for that is what needs to be done.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and in the lower part of the abdomen, it is convenient that you make the patient lie on her back, and raise her legs higher than her head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, then put the head and the buttock higher than the lower parts, and likewise the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts so that you understand that the lower part should be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and then it is necessary to treat what I say in great and painful wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds, however, you should prepare, then put your fingers between your hands and minister with them that which covers the whole rupture in your hand, and join the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common way of sutures, and it is that you should press a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a space of one thread, and put in a needle there with a strong good thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the needle, which is inside the skin, as much as you make it pierce from that part, and join together the two heads of the needle with the three together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then the strain of a double thread enters the needle from both sides, then assembles the two shoulders of the wound in front, and then leaves a space of two, and puts another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then lay the thread down as you did with the first needle, and do not cease to do so according to what you have done with the needles, until all the wound is closed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be small and large, because small needles cover all the wound, and too large ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	so that they may be small;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and do not push the needles too far from the edge of the wound and the hide, so that they do not cover and open the wound before the suturing;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cover the shoulders of the needles so that they do not wound the patient when he sleeps, and put blankets or sheets over the shoulders of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is sewn up;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of sewing with needles is more appropriate for small wounds, because it requires only one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and it is that you join the two pieces of skin together with a strong thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these three together, then remove the needle from the part where you began, in the same way that one sews clothes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a space of about half an inch between each stitch;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch is suitable for a man who had a cut or a stab, which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and it contained two palms' worth of bowels, and the wound ran into the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I took him into my care when it had been ## hours since the injury, and the wound was well-healed after fifteen days, so I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the miracle was that he died, and this was a wonder;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and do not heal it with ointment, for I am in a place where there is none to be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and do not put on any cotton wool again that day, and wash it with honey water as long as it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two proper ways to sew.
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and thread it from the outside part all the way inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the right side in the right way, so that the thread comes out on the opposite side from where you started sewing, threading the needle as you go, and piercing from the inside part all the way to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the meaning of this stitch is that you also sew as the furrier does, and leave the thread on one side, and take it up on the other, until the stitching is finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of suturing, which is properly performed by Galen, is if it is so that there is no knot, the two parts are joined together naturally, and one of the heads is applied to the other head in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	insert an awl or needle near the center, and pierce it only slightly, leaving the two heads of the wound intact;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outer side only to the inner part, leaving the two heads of the wound intact; then
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and then the other from the outer side only to the inner part, in two other places that are on the opposite sides of the wound;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the method of suturing with blood, and it is the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen says this word, and no one testifies that it should be done in such a way, that the thread has to be passed through two needles, or through each of them;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the way of those who sew with needles;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, then the stitch is stronger than the others from the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments for the wound are such as they are for other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the fire has moved it, then put back the intestine and the stitch;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder with a spreading tool, and if the fire has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound closes;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and clean the thread, and make the sutures tight, and apply the salve and the spice;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as for others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicine, put on cotton wool, so that it begins to come off, and move it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will not become commingled with the principal members, then it is fitting that you moisten another light member with oil of thyme or rose oil, and put it between the arms, and cut off the joints;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it feels pain or inflammation in the balls, and many times happens, if the cataracts of black wine are washed away, and most often the inflammation comes up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	Since you have no need of other medicine in the various preparations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will connect with the main members, then it is convenient that you wet another light one in oil of tempere or hot rose oil, and put it around the ankles, and clean out the blisters; and if it feels pain or corruption in the balls, and often happens, if the clisterize of black wine soothes, and more often the corruption comes up to the intestines; and pierce them inside, and know that when this large intestine is, it is lighter to heal than the small one.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the scar tissue jumps out of the wound, also put it back as with the intestines, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has become dry or black, then you must cut the black spot, because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the shoulder and the part of the wound to the side in order to ease the extraction when the scar tissue falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the blister
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, then it can be restored in some cases, as I have seen that an honest man was pierced or stabbed by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and there was discharge and wind;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I shall employ whatever means I can to heal him, and I shall not cease from applying a course of treatment until he is well, and I shall bind up his wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that the wound had healed, I doubted that the patient had ill in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no evil, but he delayed in better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they said no experiments that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be tied in some way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take two big testicles, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the testicles have opened the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that it draws its mouth out;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then he covers the head, and that remains in place so that it cannot be separated, and then he puts another testicle after in the same way as before, until the wound is entirely covered;
et cout la plaie.	And bind up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If it burns in the intestine, and does no harm to the patient, and can be tied with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the end of this intestine thread that is separated from the rest, and then tie it onto an end of a fine twisted linen thread; then wrap the thread around the intestine, and cut it into sections, and then remove it from the incision.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing with needles is only useful if done according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is big and wide, mostly when it is in one of the small intestine grooves, there is no medicine that can help, except with carefulness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula, whether it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	are that all wounds or abscesses, when they heal, are called 'fistula' in general, and most when they have gone through the body and come out at the other end.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the true nature of a hard and white nodule, where there is no pain, and it is also smooth like the feathers of an owl;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and once in a clear bow, and another time thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and once pock, and another time enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and it does not hurt, it is only by one of VIII causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by small amount of blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	or because of evil;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it is hard within and on the lips, so that it does not give birth to filth;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much bow;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the bones are rotten, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good for the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is in the way of poison;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late in digestion, and late in health, and runs away by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins where there are bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already explained all these reasons, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I make you aware of the treatment of fistulas, which is done by manual labor.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula can occur in all limbs of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the syphillus, or the intestine, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if there is only one that comes to the principal member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are in this way are of great difficulty, and there is only work, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no fistula that does not come to the level that I have said, and you have pledged to cure it, and you see it clearly, then take a piece of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, touch it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if it is torn, so that the search for a thin tent of throw, because the throw folds itself inside the tangling.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula is broken in two places and you cannot well search for it by tents, if it clisters through one of the breaks, because the moisture goes so quickly from one break to another, and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then search for it by your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and cut them through completely, and ask the patient very well whether he feels pain when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you know very well the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint or a nerve or an artery or a vein or any of the places that I have told you about, if it is in accordance with what I have told you, and take out the false joint and the corroded bones that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure as long as she is healed, and the fistula is very deep in a straight place, so that you cut it perfectly, as much as you can, then I put wet tents in medicine water, and bottle them up to the head of the fistula, as long as the medicine corrupts the excess that is delayed at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put honeycombs in a fine cheese cloth, as long as it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this, then the cautery as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackening, then cut it as long as the corruption is all bone, then cure with honeycombs of fine cheesecloth as long as it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if he is not cured, and bend back as before, knowing that you have not gone far from the source:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it unveils and searches until you are at the base, and removes all the corruption, then restore the position;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is thus cured, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep that you cannot come to it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is another means than to ease it by nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is one small bone corrupted, and you can pull it with pliers, if you extract it with the suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, leaving none;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture causes you to make a mistake and fear, and it becomes dry and solid, and deliver the bones;
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound something that prevents putrefaction, and let it be until the flesh has putrefied around the bones, and then the bones will come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as of a leg or thigh, if you wait until the putrefaction is all over the bone, then mend the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is much decay of it and comes to little more than the root of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is convenient to cover all of it up to the point where there is decay, and then mend it until it is set;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man of about thirty years, who had pain in his leg from a cause that entered the body, so that the matter came out to the leg, and there was a large abscess, and he had no clear cause to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the mirror by their madness turned up so high that it touched the abscesses, and consumed a great deal of matter, and became a fistula, and went out a great deal of pus and moisture from the heart.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many people were cured with it in two years, and I had no skill in the art of medicine until I was called to cure them, and I saw their leg and the medicines they used to cure themselves, and those who were cured by the pus that came out of their body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his heart became red in youth, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of those clefts, and then I searched all the clefts, and I found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	So I hastened and went into one of the pustules as far as I could see a piece of bone, and I found it corroded and eaten away, and the corruption went all the way down to the bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew what had come out of the bone, and I took care that there should be no other corruption there, except for what I had taken out.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicine by long tenors, and could not bind it;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the continuing corruption in the bone, and dried it, and then I put the bone back together, and leaned to bind the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not but that I copai an palm of the bone, and lead it away from all the molecule, then I restored it with medicine;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he was healed and bound very well, and I did not need to reopen the wound except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car por l'evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l'os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n'ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l'aleir ne a venir.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the chest, then it should be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a bandage, and stretch it out at the top of the bone that is opened, and command no one
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and join another chain of a larger length to the first one, and place it over the shoulder that is forward of the bone, and position the head, such that you drag the corrupt chain off the bone, and remove the head from above the spot where you see silk, so that the silk does not scratch the head.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and hold a stick or a wedge out of place to support the bone so as not to move the head.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to make silk visible and feelable as often as possible; and again and again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	If the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and corruption is in the middle or in part of it, then remove all of the head.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then hold out a stick out of place, and make silk run from one part to the other of the corruption, and let the silk come from the long end of the corruption, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if corruption is in the joint, then destroy the corrupted joint, and from the other side, keep the bone intact;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other pain than that of the joint;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if corruption is where the hand or foot is pricked, this is very strong, but you must still inquire about that corruption, how it hurts you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and wash it in all ways that you can, but the vein or nerve do not make you opposite;
