et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the chisel and the nails to repair these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their size and fineness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for each work there is a special tool;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and knows that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manner of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if he imagines the instrument which you have a trade according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head might be dislocated due to an abundance or deficiency of moisture, or due to heat or cold.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have medicine that corrosion by the cure of medicines, and it does not benefit, if you cover that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from death due to the malice, which is greater, of the failure of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the members become black, and that it seems to be burned by fire, and after this blackness, the corrosion of the member goes from member to member, and takes hold everywhere;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you strike with copper, and if it is due to the piercing of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and adders and others, then the corrosion is at the head of the two parts, if the copper, and does not give them space to come until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes only to the hand, if the copper has reached the joint, so that the corrosion does not come only to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, if the copper has reached the neck;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the neck, then it is death, and you will only achieve one thing by measuring its strength.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And so do not let the corrosion come to your feet:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and if it comes at the first joint, if the copper then goes beyond the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to your feet, if the copper reaches all your feet;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises up in the leg, so hit the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes up over the hip, so there is no other remedy except to make the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the way to wrap or sew the limb is that you tie it down and stretch it out, and extend one minister one of the limbs downstream, and another minister the other limb upstream, and you sever the bag which is between the two limbs at a wide gap, as far as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then wrap or sew it, and put a linen cloth on each side so that the silk does not touch the sound leg, and come to the patient with another wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if the blood rushes out when you work, then quickly cauterize the leg with some restraining powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a convenient bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to him at home on a certain day:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he had a blackness that seemed like fireburn, and this corrosion came first to the bottom of his foot, so much that it discolored all the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the honourable man saw the corrosion, he covered the whole foot with it, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after that the corrosion came again to his hand, and came to me, and I put on it things that rub, after washing the skin, and I could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he commanded me to cover his hand, and I refused, for I had hope of regaining the substance;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I doubted also that if he were to cut his hand, he would not die, for the virtue of the man was feeble;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired all, and returned to his country, and he sewed his hand up with copper, and he was cured;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have told you this only so that if you should ever need to do something else, you will know how to do it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No time comes when the abscess is in its place, and it remains so long that it causes great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it ruptures and perforates, and goes out through the belly, and remains stuck there, just as our serfs do;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is on top is as thin as silk curtains, and it does not corrode down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "clean", and is not called " fistula ";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure should be that you cut all around the skin, and most importantly when it is thin, just as we do with cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it should not be burned for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have cut the skin so that it bleeds, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thin like a sheet of cloth, then treat it with a hot water bath.
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	 observe if the breasts are large, and the breast that is affected has a foul odor, then treat it with Egyptian medicine that is made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take the following: oil and lead oxide, mix them equally, and cook them in a pot over the fire until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take this according to your need, and make it in water and honey, and harden the inside, and extract the hole;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for two hours, then extract it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this mutch times, till the sinews be broken, and the bone come out;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and no time is hardened with water of ashes, when this medicine is present, and it is that you squeeze ashes from a vine's bark, and pour water on top, then let it flow, and harden, until you know the sinews are well broken;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither can the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then harden it with a little bit of ground limestone;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you harden it with honey and wine, that the honey's property of breaking and washing is present, and the wine makes the inside sour;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you have engaged that the breasts are well changed, if the plaster of those who make them be mixed with oil and wine, and made like this:
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you clisterize it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken in the treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the chest is small, and the clister's hole does not enter, if it is widened with a little iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, as much as it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, so that the clister does not enter it by leaving a little space on either side, and if the hole where it enters is above or below the breast, so that the copers touch it;
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is drawn to its full length, if it does not leave a gap.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the bottom string as you see, so arrange in such a way that the bow runs to the lowest level where it is, for when the bow is drawn to its full length, if it does not leave a gap; and if you cannot cover the bottom string as you see, so arrange in such a way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bow runs lightly downward, and does not leave anything of the bow;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidation medicines to put on the wound, and are on a linen cloth that covers all the wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover as tightly as possible the hole on the side opposite the largest opening, since sewing together the linen cloth according to the amount of the hole, and place it on the hole on the wound in order to tighten the bow, and do not lift the large cloth before several days;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and those who are on the chest of the breastbone, often for cutting the bowels, and for what runs from the bowels, whether it is poison or pus or enough or not digested or indigestive;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and how much of the medicine has spread out and you see the nature that rises on the chest of the breastbone, know that the breasts are already irritated, and bring the medicine;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then unbind it in the morning or on the third day, and when you undo the wound, if you change another cloth, and renew the poultice.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if her breasts are swollen and painful after many days, because her breasts do not ache.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons run long after the spring, so that you are not desperate for health because healing is close.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who delay healing their wounds and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and the bowels that are not digested rise from the chest after many days, knowing that the breasts are not irritated;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if it is delayed to hear from another, and is to be postponed, then such medicines are mixed wet in substance and dried in virtue, as the ointment finishes, for there is a great part of vinegar, and this is the hind medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the dry medicine, and make it with oil of roses, and aromatize it with equal equal wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then the confit and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and that medicine makes honey cooked enriched, when the dry ointments are not present, or you take mirr and alloea and incense, and grind it, and powder it on honey as soon as it comes out of the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then put it in a glue drape, and apply it to the breast, and never administer it without an oil base, and roots of the celestial plant, which is also like flour of times and hundred;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in the use of simple substances or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	break them up, and reduce them to a fine powder, and put on honey as I have said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is prolonged, and this cure does not help, then know that corruption is complete, and it causes pain in the bone, or in the limbs, or in members;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the cure of the fistula, as we have said above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the nail of the toe
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panaritides is an abscess that may arise in the nail of the hand or foot, or perhaps in another two;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it has become infected and one does not pay attention, then it comes to an abscess, and causes great pain and heat as far as the root of the nail, and perhaps even the whole thing;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corruption extends to the bone, as much as it comes with a painful stink, and the two legs are wide apart, and the color is yellow;
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, then you must cut off all the excess that has accumulated under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The fire cautery is a great help if the bone is sound, and the fingernail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the fingernail presses down on the wound, and begins to prick, and bleeds, then you must take off the fingernail that pricks the wound, and cut it short, and carefully and lightly cut the nail edge, and put burning and corrosive medicines on it to stop all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with ointments as long as it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it and try hard, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the joint corrode, then cut it and try as hard as said above, then heal as long as it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken, and bruised, and smells of pain, then first you must heal it;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and then cut the nail of the spur with a chisel from side to side above, and be careful that the chisel does not go all the way down to the claw, because if the patient feels too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if so, put something on that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	la douleur du bras endormi de la main
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Le doigt qui pousse dans la main de certains hommes est complètement charnu, et par aventure il y a un os, et jamais une ongle, et aucun d'eux ne nait à la racine de la jointure, ou la naissance est chez certains hommes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	whoever is born in the middle of two bones does not move, and whoever is born at the joint between two bones may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the nail of him who is chubby is so light, in a certain way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it in its root with a wide chisel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	whoever is born at the root of the joint is difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	if you keep it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born between two joints, you must first chop the flesh completely around the bone; then cut the bone with a suitable knife; and finally treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together by nature, by the joining of a wound, or by the burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	if you cover that which should be joined naturally, so that the shoulder is reset according to its natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	and put between two tarpaulins or drapelets moistened with oil so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	ou tu met entre dous pièces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leis soit soudés, si com il convient.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it comes out of one of its two sides with the palm, if you hold it as it should be.
des vils	of evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	O you place between two thin pieces of felt, as long as the leeches are stuck together, just as it should be. There are large envelopes filled with melancholy excesses that come from many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more comes in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should not administer any more purging remedy, but rather treat it with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure for this is according to two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that one copes them, and draws out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size is according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	arise the first leg with very hot water, until the large sore is thin, and then draw out the leg of the sick from above the thigh down to the joint of the foot;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one place, or in two places, or in three places of a large size, then slice and draw out the black blood strongly with your hand from one end to the other as much as the virtue of the disease can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command that he be dyed with black tar;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and restart the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are empty, and pour on the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The treatment for this is done in this way:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	He should wash the patient's leg if there is hair on it, then dip or bathe it, and heat his leg with cold water until it becomes red, and the veins swell up;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	If you do not have a bath, if you heat it on the fire, and then cut the vein at the top of the shin at the knee joint, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	and soak the skin with honey, and burn the vein from each side until it feels like you are touching it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when it turns red and black, and when it enters or leaves the skin so seems to us as a white rope;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then pour out the blood until it is removed from the skin, and then tighten it with a light pinch, then cut it into two pieces.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then burn the skin on the vein until it feels like you are touching it, then loosen it with your finger, as you have done, and tighten it with another pin.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another piece, or several, if you need them, then loosen it and cut it to the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it from size to size until it is all out, then cut it off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it up, then bind a needle to the whole thread very firmly, and tie it and pull it, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, neither can you pull nor lift it up, and it causes harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have finished treating it, put wet wool covered with wine and oil on top of the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healthy again.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the eye is twisted and wrapped up together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cover it up;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and pull it as we have said above.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron where the eye breaks out is curved, and do not cut, so that it does not break the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is a heavy corbel, because if it were thin, it would tear the vein, but if it were thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm places where there are no herbs or trees, and on land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And perhaps it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and such a thing happens that the skin breaks out in a rash, as if it comes from within the body, creeping and winding its way between the skin and the bone.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this disease are that it comes to the leg a very great inflammation, then the places change, and the vein begins to come out, also as a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head is opened, if you wrap a piece of gauze around it from one and a half to two inches, and then bandage it to the leg, and every time there is no more of it, so wrap the gauze and bandage.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too far away, so take a part of it, wrap it up again, and do not cover the rest as far as it comes out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you do this, get back into the cart, and cause infection and pus where it is, and bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of which thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the throat, and nothing remains there or corrode.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and never once has this hand been treated when it was as long as X, or longer than X, and one hundred and ten years old at most, and when you cut it, if you bottle or pierce it, and pierce it up to the bone, so that everything goes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the matter that is inside become empty, and introduce at its place medicines causing pus no day, then heal it as you do with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	and never once has this hand rained, and least of all when it opens at the ankle joint or the foot, and it rains much from it, and it jumps out.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure the dislocations as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that hatch between leather and cart
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our country "beef disease", because it often affects the bulls, and is a small worm that emerges between the skin and the shell, going up and down all over the body, making holes where it goes, and jumping out again;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is infected with pus-like humors, such as come from worms, beetles, maggots and parasites;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and there is doubt about its malignity, because when it goes through the body and rises to the head, and comes to the eye, it may turn back and destroy the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him cure and draw out, you can do nothing except when he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then it is necessary that you lay him on a firm tie tightly, then turn him over and draw him out hard, and turn his body inside out, and you will not find him, so burn him with fire all over, until he dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm it does, if it turns the oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	If you see the head of the shoulder near the oil, then hold back the dislocation with your hand, and push down hard;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and the patient should use medicines that dissolve the bad humors, and wash with meat juice that is rotten;
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a painful disease that affects some limbs and spreads from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I poked it again, and saw it go up as high as a worm does to the shoulder, quicker than anything else, like silver in motion when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain left that place, and then it came into the shoulder, and soon after it spread throughout the whole body, until it reached the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me that it twisted again around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how much this woman was moving her member from one to the other, for I had never seen such a thing with this disease.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I had often heard that such pain can move from one part to another, but as I saw it in the woman's case;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought that perhaps because her chest was tight and the veins were visible, and perhaps because of the constricted windpipe;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And I didn't see any reason for this in those who are healthy, whose chests are moist and whose veins are relaxed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	When you treat this disease and the patient feels that pain, if it comes again as we have said, let him lie down and keep him there until the constriction in the windpipe eases;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you don't see the hair, if the doctor who removes the wind with pills of rotten fruit, and pills of nettles, and similar things.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the places where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity is that it is those who have large tips, small, hair, and soldered;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those who have two angles, and of those who have tongues, and of those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which does not move in any member so moves according to two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in a principal member it chieres as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore chieres in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you hereafter, then you know it:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so that you wash yourself from the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after many preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign is not apparent to you, and the arrow has not been fully extracted, if you pull it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the skull when the arrow breaks and pierces the bone, and the wound is near the skull, is when there is a splitting and crushing and twisting and pain in the joints, and inflammation and swelling and pain in the tongue, and muscle spasms and confusion of thought, and vomiting of food;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it is not from the nose, or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is not from the throat or voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and in salt water there seems to be pus and it smells like burnt meat;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then hold back from the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it scratches or pricks is that it is near the left breast, and also smells as if it were stuck in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and for fear it moves too, like a chicken, and with short breath and coldness comes and faints.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	For then you must know that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes is that it does not ooze pus from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he gasps for breath and shivers with cold. So you should know that death looms.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow pierces through the skin and the bone, it is painful to touch the spot;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and sorrowful sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and moves all the limbs of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters the stomach, for fear that some of the meat is not digested.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters the abdomen and does not exit through the intestine, then there is no hope for recovery or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, and the urine flows out in spurts, causing the patient to urinate and feel great pain;
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	For that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member - the face and throat and shoulder and arm and spine and leg and foot, and similar limbs - are saved according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and does not cause venom, tell me how you would do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man who had an arrow pierce his throat and tear at the root of his neck;
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and took off the fat of the ear with a sharp blade, and was healed without feeling any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And throw an arrow that it falls in the grease of oil from paper dried, and the arrow was re-laid, and could not but the tip towards the fur, and it was the arrow great by an arch-turquoise, all I made to hear without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the game was sane, and came no bad accident.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And threw an arrow into the throat of a Christian, and it was the arrow Arabic to ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loved the beards, and subtle as I threw it, and was sane the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And throw an arrow at the heart, that it was the chewed or stomach, and thought he died;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that it passed XXX days, if did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and engaged it, and threw it hard, and came no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish for a man who has an arrow in his chest or back, and the wound is seared above it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and delay the arrow within him, and do not hinder his natural dispositions, nor find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I have another man, to whom an arrow has fallen into his face, and the wound is seared;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and so he delays not to suffer great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And there was a man of the king's prince, whose arrow had gone astray and struck him in the neck, and he was slightly 기울 to the left side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was all turned around.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat after that which had been hit three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I wanted to give it all my care, and I did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a piercing pain and pain in his left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I put on the plaster with the medicinal herb, so that the legs do not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the leg of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on both legs, and quickly healed the wound, and delayed it for a long time, so that the patient felt the arrow in his neck;
et il le me dist.	and he took it off.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put the corrosive medicinal paste on the wound, and tried it, and felt the tip of the arrow getting warmer at the joint;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted the opening of the wound with the corrosive medicinal paste, until the head of the arrow was clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and the wounds heal well within three months, and then he opened the wound where I had tied the thorns, and stretched it from one side to the other, and could not draw out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I ceased not to study and invent methods of instruments until I had obtained good hooks; according to what their form will be at the end of this chapter, I fixed them on, and repaired the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judged that the cartilage in the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I repaired it then, and sewed up the wound, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I have not told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your treatment on what I did not say, for the book cannot take everything into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the master physicians compare very little to what is present and failing, truly nine operations and nine instruments, at the dismemberment of strange things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows are of members where they are stuck except for two ways.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which is shot out by an arrow, is a transfixed arrow in its flesh, and never remains in one place now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go out now, if you leave the flesh rotten within, and the hole is healed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot go out, if you leave it like that for some days, and move every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it goes out, and if it does not go out, if you pierce within all the way up to a small hole, as long as the flesh within is stretched out, and then you let it go;
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes down to one of the vents of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said can happen to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If not extracted, but left until it is even after a few days, because if the arrow comes to the sinew, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the shoulder bone, and does not come to the syfac, and the patient remains for some days without any bad accident, then use the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if she is wet and cannot be extracted, if you administer tar for her, as I told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the joint until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is stuck in the center, if it cannot be seen, seek it with all your strength;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if you extract it with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot extract it by the wound, and by the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, then cut off as much of the wound as possible;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to hold it in place, remove the bar that is stuck on both sides as far as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully although you do not break the arrow, that you draw it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot hold it once, then let it go until it is no longer painful, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the healing does not go well, bring what we have said in this chapter regarding the treatment with its paint;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and guard against cutting the nerve and the vein, and do not draw out the arrow with danger, soon or slowly, firmly or loudly;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and put the patient in the position he was in when the arrow entered, for that is the greatest help, and if you cannot do that, then follow the signs that the wound shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another way, where it does not open anything, or if the skin is swollen in a certain place, whether we see it or not:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut off then, as long as the pliers can take them, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	If you jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round, as far as it enters into the bone and broadens the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she can't get out, keep her there for a while longer, and then start the extraction process again until she finally comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if he is stuck in the arrow, push him hard.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if he is stuck, you need to push him hard. If you push him with an instrument, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hole of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push away, and if the arrow is stuck, you push the instrument with a sharp point to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has touched something, it is necessary that you cut away all of the flesh around where the poison is; if you can do so, then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	and if the arrow is stuck in the neck or the stomach or the bladder or the ribs, and it is coming out, you can cover it up. If you cover it up;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and don't forget to cover the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound. This is work for a doctor.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treatment until they are well.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the clamps used to treat arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the piercing knife used is similar to an owl's feather, to pierce the tip of the arrow, as here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the clamps for piercing and for extracting, if it is this, is:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of the veins of the torso, common:
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	For veins that are healed are XXXI, where there is a head of XVI, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two batons which are after the ears, which are called "dous herbech".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two temples appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in two nostrils of two hairs, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is under the brow;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the head of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two arteries which are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and they are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are dislocated from the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	the veins that are commonly spoken of are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cerebral vein, and it runs down on the left side, and it is called by lay people "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cerebral and basilic veins, and it is called by lay people "vein of the wrist";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein lies on the right side, and it is called by lay people  "vein of the abdomen", and it is under the fascicle, and this is the one that is spoken of, which opens clearly over the breastbone.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the jugular vein is the vein that lies between the thumb and the index finger, and if it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and where the foot is there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one if it is dislocated at the top of the left side pocket on the coast of the rib cage, and the second one which is at the ankle of the right leg.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called «nesse», which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins dislocated from those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	the vein that is called «sainte», which is after the ears if it helps the old catarrh, and has a headache;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the saint, as I told you, is that you remove the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a sharp cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then pull the patient's neck with a twist, until the two veins appear behind the ears depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	keep them then in your two hands, and where you feel the pulse of one side dislocated, if it is a sign of pain;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and take the needle, and pierce through the vein up to the bone, and then lift your hand back all the way up, and cut and strip the flesh and the vein well, you must travel through it all, and let blood as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then extract and bind, until it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The two arteries that are in the two temples, so it is the age of the elderly, and the sight is dimmed, and the eyes are used to tears;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the seer is so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient extracts his neck, until the two veins open;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse of your two fingers, and then sign with a knife;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then place the blade against the vein at the top of your index finger, and point it downward, and place the blade against the vein, and cut, just as you did in the other two veins, and pour blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then remove the bandage from the patient, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form the shape, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of their treatment and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting from the forehead is as effective as that from the temple for the treatment of old diseases of the face and headaches, and for migraine;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient twists his neck so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called a "seeder", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the neck of the patient, and tie the vein tightly until it is healed, and do not use a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not necessary for the flame to be too hot;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and heal across, because the bone is close together, and the flame may break if it is too narrow.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The two veins that are in the two laminae should be cauterized with oil, and with the tan, and with the redness, and with the blight in the oil, and with the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their healing is that the patient's neck is drawn out by twisting it with a cord, as has been said;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	and then the medicine, and let the mediciner go through, a little of the long flame a little wide, because there is no fire.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is thin, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make the blood run, as much as you need to, and then put it on cotton, and put it well on.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The medicine of the vein of birth if it is good for acute fever and sudden sickness, and for face diseases, as headaches and pain that comes to the face, and indeed when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the medicine is that the patient strangles his neck, then bring the fire's thin flame to the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well on its own, and the blood will begin to run now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and don't burn too much, and make the blood run according to your need, then let it sit for a night, because it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	is the treatment of two kinds of fever, and also with the use of cautery, and many diseases, and pemphigus, and corrosives, and herpes, and are considered.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	is the quality of the medicine that is that the patient extracts his neck from one side to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master standing over the patient's chest, and the patient cutting a long vein, then treating it with blood in moderation, or as much as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then make another in the other vein, then tie up the arteries, and extract them slightly, so that the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the animals
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Of the health of the lips, that they may not hurt themselves when eating in the mouth, and do not corrode the gums, nor tear the lips, nor cause pain or disease in them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the cure is to make the patient sit in front of you, and to tie his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then tie them both, and if you don't recognize them and are in doubt, tie the larger one of each pair, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is a similar method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	the cure for the veins that are above the tongue after the cure of the cerebral vein, and it is at the extraction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the healer is that the patient dies between your hands in front of the sun, and he lowers his tongue, and looks down on everyone a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then heal them both, and do not be too confident, for arteries are fragile.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the leg, which are commonly treated, are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or burn them all with a strong fire, or apply a subtle olive oil as thin veins are called "aneasil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and thickness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the sharp, thick blade is called a 'flame', and it is wide as you see it.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And one should be skilled in opening flat-headed veins that contain thick blood and trouble;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	This is the form of the olive oil fire:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle pointed, and is to save the veins that are subtle, where there is subtle blood citron.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healer of the base, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that affect the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon that he heal the wound, and that he wash with water that is hot.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he stops the artery, and the blood comes running out, if it is necessary to stop the bleeding, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be pricked with fire but cut off like a nail;
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the nail does not open clearly, you must extract it, and change it for another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you do not want any rain of it, or you heal in its place the vein at the base of the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut off with fire like we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you can see the place of the wound, then it is necessary that you extract the arm, and touch the place as much as you can feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	and then sign the neck of the chest, and then tie his arms, and cut the vein from the flame with a sharp knife.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to hurt yourself in the artery when you see the neck dislocated, because it is the artery:
eschui la donques.	so avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see coming out on top as urine from a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	so hurry up, and put your finger on top of it for a long time, then open your finger so that the blood does not flow, because it often happens:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	tie his arms, and leave them like that, and do not move the patient.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be afraid, and do not move him until he is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood does not stop flowing and he bleeds, cut the artery, because the head of the shoulder is pulled back:
et estainche li sans.	and they stop breathing.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fir tree, and burn it, and take one half and put it on well until the other day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if they stop breathing, it is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, if the doctor, as we have said, with powders that stop breathing;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of breath is not done in many places for the small size of the wound, and the power of the vein of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein that comes out in the middle should be treated so that it stops bleeding from the top of the head and from the base of the neck, for it is composed of basilic and cerebral veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the doctor should be warred against the vein that comes out at the back of the neck, and if he cuts too much in perfection, the blood will flow from the nerve, and it will swell up and the patient's health will be broken, and perhaps will not heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any men for its subtility, then you must cut off the limb with the saw.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two necks, then cut it short.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The removal of the cephalic nerve if it helps, that it does not move with the head, and aid the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to cut with fire at the olive or at the water fire, for this is the most saved of all veins, because it does not have a nerve nor an artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, you must choose the lighter way, and do not grieve anything if it fails the first time, and you start again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the leg does not hurt in any men the first time, but it does not grieve anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about removal, if it is not done except to preserve health and avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the soldier be made in one of the three veins that are or cut.
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	this is to say, cephalic, fast and basal;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and the soldier must be made in the beginning of fasting, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and the soldier must be made on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
