Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The soldier who is administered with medicines has no determined urination, but that when the need arises, whether it is day or night, at all hours and in all seasons;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and does not fit to make the children until they are twelve years old, and a woman except for four months after giving birth until she is seven months pregnant.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	The patient who is free from disease does not have a determined time limit, but when it comes to eating or drinking, it is in all hours and at all times; and one should not heal children until they are 12-13 years old, nor women who have been pregnant for less than four months until they are seven months pregnant. One should not heal the elderly who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when some must be made, in whatever way, it is necessary that he empty the bowels of a light enema, if there is retenes moisture, so that the veins do not attract the excess of noxious matter harmful to the main members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k'il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d'abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l'arme ou dou cors;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly the humors, for him shall be fat, through meat and drink and medicine, if you have such power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter or bathe, for nothing will benefit him, to subtilize his blood, and heal him of the vein at the pit of the stomach from within the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep yourself from work, from hunger, from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be quiet and still, and let the surgeon be higher than you who heals, and rub his arms twice or three times, then pull the ligature gently, for when it is too tight or short, it cannot run;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the cut with hands, until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the surgeon's flame with a spot of old oil, and then put his left hand on that vein to stop the bleeding, so that the vein does not break and bleed;
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee from the surgeon like strings, and some that are prone to bleeding, so that when one puts the flame on them, if one takes it away, the vein does not open, and thus one is of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens a vein, if the wound is too narrow, for in these things it is necessary that the patient be warned.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if he opens the vein for the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then start again a little bit further on that line or above hospital, if the leach is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the leech is inflamed and the patient hopes, let him be left for a day or two, and do not bandage his arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	so that there will come abscesses;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter or bathe again, and then start the treatment again if he wants:
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the dislocation is small, or the joint is slightly subluxated and you doubt that it will move as much as you see, then firmly in the same joint to all the flame right:
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little surgery, so that the veins are swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the vein swollen, do not stop the bleeding, and put a little oil on it, because it cools the body of blood, and it is soft in this place where the oil is;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil to each vein that you are suturing in order to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this also makes the wound and the incision look better and smaller when it is put on it;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so that the hole is small and does not spread if it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there is an abscess that comes out often, especially when the opening of the vein is small, do not hurry and put wet sponge on it with a little heat and hold it in place for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it stays in place for a few days without any black or green, then it does not harm me;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on nothing but aloe or myrrh, juice of calamus, marjoram, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often an abscess and appearance to the disease of the temple:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	So then put your hand on it, and if you feel that the place is soft by the pressure of your hand, then this is the appearance of evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	So avoid putting on anything we have said, because perhaps at the root of the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but the plaster dry to harden the place, then treat it with other treatments until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And each person should be treated according to the quantity of his virtue and the color of his blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the root is black, let it go out as long as it is red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see a lump, let it grow until it is small.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are ill and need bloodletting, let them make the wound larger and wider the flames;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for those who are weak, do the opposite, and let them bleed little and often, and they should bleed across rather than into; do not bleed them in a piercing manner.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	This method of bleeding is safe from the destruction of blood and the stretching of nerves, and it is better than long or broad bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for those whose hearts need to be bled, give them wet juice from pomegranate seeds;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if it is hot, three or four times; and if it is of cold complexion, before the bleeding give wet juice made from muscatel grapes, or honey-scented syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cumin, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it is the case that one has had a bout of diarrhea after eating bread made with three or four times the normal amount of grape juice, then it is right to drink beer and subtle, fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if one farts with the arms raised up and then begins to vomit at another time, when he is weakened by great vomiting, that he heal little by little, according to the quantity of his continuing virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to vent his arms after the first wound, and he has a strong cord, so that he heals seven hours after the first wound, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be wounded elsewhere, should be healed in two days or three.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has a fever that is hot inside the body, and brings forth heat.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and widen the hole as much as possible;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then you shall treat all the conditions of sickness, and place your hand on his pulse as he recovers, that death does not come to him in place of recovery, and that this happens many times, when the recovered person is neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not necessary when you see the shoulder dislocated that you make him sneeze a second time, and the hole is closed, that you press firm upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	not if he is curved, that he extends his arm carefully, for that would be ill;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him alone until he recovers a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you place the tip of the flame upon it so that the blood that is frozen at the dislocation of the vein comes out, and put there a little string soaked in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, let it go and do not tighten it, as long as the abscess is calm.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires to drain the blood a second time, if it is in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is attached to the vein from which blood comes out.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way of treatment is that the patient dips his hand in hot water until the pulse is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then cut with care so that the vein shows clearly, then treat now from above, not from the sides nor from the back;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And make the hole wide, and treat well near the joint of the hand, and it cannot be taken out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood run in the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it has been cut, do not dip the hand in hot water again, for we dip it more when it is healing than when it is cut;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the treatment of this vein is safer than any other vein, as there are no arteries or nerves involved.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The treatment for all liver diseases with the right hand is as follows:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Estrain the hand, and dip it in hot water, until the vein is gone, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and split it from side to side, and cut it all around, if it doesn't hurt anything;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and don't cut it too much in detail, for the nerve is all exposed and then put the hand back in hot water, if it gets stuck in the wound, and cannot be taken out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, put oil and wax on it to make it strong; and do the same for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the left hand is good for the disease of the heart, and do the same as I told you before for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve for the foot is good for all kinds of diseases that come from the body, such as diseases of the bride, and restraining of flowers, and old diseases of the feet and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of the wound is that the patient dips some foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it stops, and puts on the joint at the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein if it is at the ankle, and then go up to the foot with many drops;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	治 the joint or more wide rain, or at the ankle, so you don't get hurt.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it on the foot, beware of the toes that are dry, and treat it also across as in sowing.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the fire go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot get it out, put the foot in water, and leave the vein well open.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you treat it for the first time, if you begin again on top of it a little bit after, because the leg is cold;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same for the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The blood vessels are at the ankles, and the pain in the knee joint is due to the blood leaving the leg when it is cut off.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of the treatment is that the patient enters or bathes, and removes from the ankle IV nails by twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then treat it in all ways that you can, and crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and wait until you have sown it, because the leg is warm, and it has been well respired by many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, let there be no rain from him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the small toe, and guard against the heels.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make so much blood flow that you see it, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and tighten it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	and now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	ventose
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuums are made of horns, or of horn, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and the vacuum is made according to two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by wounding and sucking up blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suction that is without wounding is according to two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is all fire, or it is without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the suction that is made by wounding and sucking up blood is made in 12 parts of the body, so that one is all in the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the other two are on either side of the collar;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the ventouse (a suction device) from the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the ventose from the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventose on the arms;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction devices on the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suction devices on the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suction devices on the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction treatment does not cause blood loss, unless it is a small vein that is spread out over the body, and for this reason it cannot be used; if it were done in the same way as a vein is treated in surgery.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	ne can be used either at full speed or at a slow pace, nor in any disease that comes from overconsumption, until the whole body is free of water.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, because of necessity or habit, we must use suction, let us do so every hour in the first half of the month, and then at the end, and also every 10 days, gradually increasing it;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they have work to do with wind, become very heavy.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who, through the hot wind, get redness and pain in their face, and in their head, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who, after blowing, have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue has fled, and are thirsty for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who dream, and see vision, and hear, and die, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and in particular when it is the middle of the month, we order them to belch after three hours from day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The danger of the wind to the head ... which comes with the eyes and does not come until all the blood has been evacuated from the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this wind-blowing is in the place of the headache of the head, and does not come until those who are of a cold constitution use it, or who have had a fever, for that does them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and so it is not fitting that I should keep you awake when you are using it, or those who have a chief cold disease.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are recovering from it often become confused, and for this reason the suction cup should be placed a little further downstream due to the doubt of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The wind and heat are in the place of the neck and base of the skull, and for this reason they cause extraction of the tooth, and cutting of the canal of the gums, and itching, and filling.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and so it is necessary to press it in, for if it holds too tightly, then it will cause pain or injury to the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The wind and heat are in the neck region, causing pain in the head, blindness and dizziness, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and are in the place of the base of the skull.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is fitting that you command the doctor to press his hand upon it, so that he does not cut the artery, and does not cause movement of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The windings of the throat are affected by disease of the mouth, and corrosion of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in the area of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wind-puctions of the shoulders cause a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The windings of the arms are affected as much as three veins of the arms, because they attract blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the patient that he not cut too deeply, for his vessels are naked of cover, and know how to cut the nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The windpipe that is on the chest is affected by diseases from the fundament, and similar diseases, and it is necessary that the windpipe be large, and of air, that it has the function of good breathing;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and if it is thin, then it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The legs' windpipes open widely, because they attract blood from all the body, and are the cause of ancient pains in the kidneys, and of the womb, and of the bladder, and cause the flowers to return;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in the second place of the feet, and of the toes, and yet they weaken the heart after a long time, and bring about many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of putting on the suction cup is that you put it first in place, and suck it quickly, and put it there firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the color of the heart red and inflamed, and notice the pain of the wound;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then take off the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the hearts, for there are some who have bitter character, and clear ones:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to wound even once, and to make deep wounds, and a little bit deeper:
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the man is fat, then it is necessary to wound him twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time for subtlety the way of blood big.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it is very thick, then you must wound a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw blood little by little, then we only have to press firmly once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want to draw blood, then we must begin again often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then we must press firmly and fully, and the end should be that the piercing is sudden, and for those who have hard and dry skin, you should wet the leather with oil that opens and dissolves:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in a place of salt, of olive oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil:
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the eye, with oil of watercress, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the overflow is thick and cold, then take oil of almonds, or of balm, or oil of anise, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the patient's skin is very dry and scaly, then one should not use oil, but it must be washed after the wound has healed with rosewater, or cold water, or water from mulberries, or water from cucumbers, or water from porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have too much moisture, if it comes out like this, or with water from myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great excesses stand up with wine of oak, or water of thistle, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or others similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and they should not be washed with a vacuum before the bath or in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and they should not sleep after vacuuming, and it is necessary that he warm himself up when he needs to be vacuumed and when he has been vacuumed;
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard those who are being treated for colitis, and their bowels are too strong and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if he needs to drink cold things, such as pomegranate, endive, and lettuce leaves in vinegar, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and sweeten them with honey, and cheese, and meat that is moist.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a pale complexion, if they drink syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and sweeten them with honey, and with honey and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on days when he feels better, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is good to give some people twice or three times the usual amount of ale or musk before or after the wind-up, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be careful with the wine, but it is good that those who are warm drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The wind-up that does not hurt are those put on the liver, and the neck, and podagre, and the belly, and the bum, and the knees, and the ankles, for this limb does not suffer to be hurt on the outside, and we put it on the breasts when it is not well;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscous substance that is in the limb, as we put wind-ups on the belly and the bum to strengthen the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an operation or a stone, if it is removed by its attracting virtue from the operation, or removes the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and so let him do as follows when he puts it on the liver and on the mouse if there is wind held back, and these windpumps are empty with just enough air to blow.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and never are they put together fire, and no times the water of the river is not emptied, if as in the disease of pleurisy, and in such a way that the windpump is filled with hot water or water in which he has boiled herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup is administered to fire as such:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has II fingers wide and half a palm in length, and is placed around the middle with a small opening, just as to fit an needle, and is made of brass, so that it does not burn the patient when put on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the middle has a bar of brass or iron, so that a clump is taken up, and are great and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For children's suckers are different from old ones, and leaner than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this sucker on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the wax candle or thread and put it through the hole in the center of the suction cup so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and these two should be at the bottom that we have said, so that when you break it, if there is steam, and then remove the suction cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the thread as before, and restart it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup that is amended in disease of pleurisy, to all water, has no hole or break, and is amended only when it is plain of water, and is put on the limb as little as possible.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	are not increased in size except for limbs that cannot be fitted with suction cups due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar things;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the naked legs of a horse, such as two or three-year-olds, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the use is that when you find swells that are in clear, flowing water free from pollution, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in clear, flowing water until they are well-fed and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then is cleansed from the wound and the suction cup, and then rub the limb until it is red, and place the swells on them;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they have healed and are cheerful, and if it can take a suction cup, it is placed on it, for that is worth more afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise up the bed, then water, very well, and then press.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the bed is too high after the heart of the body, then dip the sheet in cold water and put it on, until the heart is dry.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are many hearts, then put on vitriolic powder or gall, and similar things, until they are dry.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you may put half of peeled peas on the bed, and let them burn there at the heat, now they will be dried.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take another heart.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the hearts do not take shape, then rub the bed with cold blood, or you may put an needle there until the heart burns, and then put them on, and sometimes when they feel the blood, they will burn.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see them chattering, if powder on a little aloe and seared, or ash, if they chatter now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapters on this chapter are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, o ignorant one, that the wise man will pour this paste on himself, which no ancient book or letter has ever mentioned.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is strange to us in our land, for I never found any good of it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and know nothing about it, except for the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much and treated the science, and by experience, and by habit, and by my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this paste what is contained therein, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly set forth the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in these two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in this book the sums of words and the chapters where the sage places his understanding, and delays on truth, so that those who are proved may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twists or strain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to save the sick person on one side and the other, if nothing else stops you, so as not to weaken the corset, or entangle it, or grow old;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or its tension is too loose or too tight.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and do not drink too much wine, nor drink any greasy foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you are sure of the warmth of the abscess, or of the spreading of the substance in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the sick person returns to his normal state of health under your care;
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed with meat that is very fat, or with viscous food, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and beans, and pies, and porridge made from veal, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar foods.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a slow healing will be delayed and slower the break will heal.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old and decrepit people cannot be healed or made strong again by their own nature because of the loss of members, nor those which are too tender, as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but doesn't heal, go up on the broken bone and thick tendons that hurt and join the limb together again, as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and doesn't do his job at all, and for this reason he needs to grow large amounts of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breakers are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break in the head is different from the break in the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the root, and another in grinding, as when one trims the tip of a feather to write with it.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if a break is with a wound, and a break is all a little crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its own tool for repair, and its own special method, according to what comes to mind in his memory;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the broken bone is known by how twisted it is, and opens well from the outside, and is pressed together by the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or misalignment, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can also have twisting, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come after this, and then now restrain it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that has happened in the middle of the joint, and are the two parts separated, it is now necessary to make them even, so that the scar comes out straight;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if the abscesses are hot, if he does not leave it for a day, as long as the abscesses are quiet.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it on the fire as soon as possible and cut it with a sharp knife, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of that which has pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then tighten it, as it will come loose again later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is joined by two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or a small member, or a string, or a cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member back in its natural position, so that when the broken parts of the member are healed, you remove all the additions by fire as soon as possible, and be careful not to cause any additional pain or injury to the patient with your work.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and set well the two bones together according to their best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	and feel with your hand whether it seems to you that it is not well
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it feels good, and do not pull too much, nor press so hard as those who work with an abscess make the member hot and contractile, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	and when the member is in order, teach the patient to keep it still, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning over, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the member be so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when there is no pain, if it is not in order, and you should put it in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep in mind that it be placed correctly, so that twists do not come when it is reset;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken members are different in smallness and greatness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	Because there are small limbs, like arms and legs and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so that one covers them with soft and thin linen cloth;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those who are fat, like thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so that one covers them with a wide and hard linen cloth, because the wide linens embrace the entire large member and hold it evenly so that there is no gap:
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	and then tie it lightly, three or four times according to the member, and tighten the linen around the hand, then go up over the break and tighten it less, so that the break then comes away a little:
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen a little at a time until you press a lot of the skin, then take another linen and tie it very tightly over the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	And then return to the part of the shoulder from the break, and hold it gently, not too strong or too lightly, as we have said in the first hour above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the ligatures of linen or drapery, until it is completely even, and then tie it all together with a bendage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	If there is an abscess or swelling, place something soothing on the abscess to soothe it and let the swelling go down, and leave it like that for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then set it upon your splints, and be they of half a pole-length of rope, or of a beam from which chisels are made, or of palm branches, and be they according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	However, it is necessary that the splint that one sets upon the break be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and so long as the member is small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it by the joints also as you did with the first line, then tie it together in advance, like in the first line on the breaking.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	then the tighter the better; and then a little looser;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the thread should be fine, not too thick nor too thin, and made of linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is too thick, like I have seen in the work of some foolish people who make their ligatures with linen twine, and that is a great mistake, because the ligature cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should be less than two inches of space between each joint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is stabbed by the chisels of the stiles after the extraction in their healthy places, then set them with a linen patch or another clean cloth so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the suture is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not convenient to extract all the members of the broken limb on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it is not good to put in joint before five or seven days, or more according to your judgment of the abscess heating up suddenly;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and show us the way of the ancient plasterers to restore fractures, dislocations, and torments:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and this is what you take from the flour that clings to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plasterer restoring fractures in many ways, especially for women and small children, because there is no too short or too long.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of plastering to restore fracture, dislocation, and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take Z abarices, and Ladaniya, and Enule, and Asafetida, and Indian gum, and Moghrat, in X z;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Mirra and Aloes, in V z;
alechil VIIII З.;	Aloes, in VIII z;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and reduce it to powder, and mix it with plenty of egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the man's complexion is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly heals broken bones, benefiting many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of using plaster that benefits twisting:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mold and beeswax, half-and-half;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Sandalwood and holly leaves, eight parts;
acaice VI З.;	Resin, six parts;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Grind well, and mix with strong wine or water, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to make plaster for joints and bones that have come out of place, so as to soothe the pain immediately, and to fix the size of the break:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take another new thing, and moisten it well with warm oil, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Do not return to bed until they have healed completely; it is good for soothing an abscess, and properly relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to make plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves, and earth-pavement leaves, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make an ointment for healing bone breaks and alleviating pain left over from abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the roots of marsh mallows, chamomile, violets, flour of vesce, of each one a part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind them, and mix it with wine, and warm the members, and mix it with water of coriander or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make an ointment that is stronger than the first one, which is used when the pain from the abscess lasts for a long time and needs to be healed quickly.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take the roots of marsh mallows, and flax seed, and hollyhock, and milkwort, and dogbane, and violet flowers and chamomile, of each one a part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind them, and mix it with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras says that one should not put anything on a broken member before the scar tissue is formed, except for a wax and oil cerote, and nothing else, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to me that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things that are a little warm, such as mirr, and aloe, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of making an ointment that is useful for injuries and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take moss and hair of the beard, or feathers of an owl, and marsh mallows, and mix them together evenly, grind them, and make an ointment and spread it on his chest.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then let it rest for a little while, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor does his bone move from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not rest by hand for days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain or itching comes to the place, or if it swells, do not delay, and dislodge it, and apply the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea water, and dip it in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on another dry cloth, wet with spring water or rose oil, and tie it to a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is warm;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and let rest the inflammation of the member, and be relieved of the pain, then begin again gently, and a little plaster, and do not pull it so hard as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and carefully as long as it is sound.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is warm and red and painful and swollen all over, and you need to apply ointment and bandages, then if it starts again, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	If the limb does not respond to any of the above treatments, only then should it be dislocated after three, four, five, or seven days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leave it for more than 20 days, according to what we have seen, until the break becomes visible and the joint comes closer to the shoulder;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then pull harder on the second, and fatten his flesh as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see that it is not necessary to reset the shoulder, know that it will not come back on its own;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then dip the shoulder in hot water each time you dislocate it, every third day, and leave it soaked for a short while;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this treatment the rebound should be prevented from happening again to the limb, and carefully restore any deformity that has occurred;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is bad, and if it is over-anxious, and I see no other thing but to allow it to relax and do it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various ways of breaking.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaking, and various shapes, and the causes are different;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures that are made by the impact of a spear, and the collarbone is broken all the way down to the shoulder which is dislocated, like a hat or it was before;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this manner of breaking is called "fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the spear pierces the bone from above and is called in this way "absolute fracture";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And it is the wound of these two great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a percussion within, or a split or a collar of stone, or a fall on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing breaking, which approaches to the tendon that is out of the socket, or which is upon the bone, and this wound is great or little.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if a wound that is healed in the bone is as fine as a hair, and is called in this way "capillary fracture";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is caused by a stone, or by falling, or by some other thing, and a piece of bone enters it, and the bones are bent so as to form a knot, like the smith when he works on the kettles;
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the stone inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens to those who have their chins wet with a wound, so that the bone is bent like a child's chin;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and in all these ways of breaking that small pieces are made which are like dice;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	I will speak to him in his own language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways to break it by pulling on them, and by the investigation, and by the rotten cart which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is caused by the fact that when we uncover the bone, and we rub it from above, if we open the black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for a fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of feeling, stiffness, palms, fever, hair becoming long and red, and other similar signs in various dispositions, so cannot be cured by doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a possible accident, and you expect salvation, begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the break comes first to you, and it is in winter, so it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourth day at most.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, so you hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the bone's thread does not corrode, and the accident that we have mentioned comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone of the fracture comes up to the hair that covers the skull, then you should split the part that is split thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you should press the chin of the sick person so as not to move it, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on top of the wound more than a hand's width, since the blood comes out at the place where the skin is separated from the bone, or an abscess; help him with what is needed, and fill the space with wet towels dipped in oil and rosin;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscess has subsided, and be sure to prevent blood loss.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to cut into the bone, and it is done according to two ways of working:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is that you chop with a narrow blade in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then another way is more grant than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	the second way is that you have a number of different blades, some narrow and others wide, some pointed, and all made of iron:
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in working lightly, so that you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is tough and hard, it is necessary that you pierce into it, so that you introduce the blades with care, not making them completely round so as not to pierce through the bone itself, and there should be a notch or a circle on top of the blade, so that it does not go through the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and there may be many consequences, so that each comes to its place in the center of the bone, so that you have time for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three ways to slow down:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing inside the bone is that you place the retainer on the bone, and turn it back two times as long as you feel the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then remove the retainer to another part a little way away, and do it all around, then cut out the space of the bone that is between the perforations, and do it more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take the bone in your hand, or any of the tools you have, such as pliers, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and make sure you do not touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone pierced and treated, if it seems to you that you should rest the edge of the bone, which is delayed from the bone by all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more tender and thinner than the other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it does not lag behind any small bones or scales, if the bone is lightly cut with tools;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then heal the wound with tent and oil that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other way to work if it is that which Galen says, which is more dangerous;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the loa very strong, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, where the break opens, so that when you have discovered that part, you put on the end of this lens-shaped incision, from which it takes its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and this side is wet in two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then forge with a small mallet above, so that you lightly chip the bone all around, and take good care of the chisel that is discolored;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is a fracture to the bone, then let it be light, for the bone that is well-healed does not cause pain and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone does not break through the skin, and the bone is cut so little from above, and there are small pieces, then cover them with a thin rasper, of which you must have various quantities, to apply in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have several thin rasers, and then more fine ones, and do not stop doing this as long as it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair losses and subtle cuts, you must bring together the cause according to its position;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	This is not easily answered by anyone who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the syphilus is discovered, then let you take a linen bandage, according to the quantity of the wound, and oil in it and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another bandage doubled II or III times, and oil in it and wine, and put it on the first bandage; then let you bind it up tightly with a band;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do it as lightly as you can so that you do not aggravate the syphilus, then bind it with one more linen bandage, and do not strip it off before it has healed the wound completely;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it so for a day or two, until the abscesses have become calm, then remove it, and administer medicines as roots of licorice, and flour of almonds, and incense powder, and aromatic wine, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer it again with powerful medicines without stinging;
