et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard that the wound is clean, so you do not leave it oozing, nor do you let any bowels assemble on the cloth of the skull, for if they corrode and penetrate, they cause great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one applies a mordantic substance, it may burn from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Watch out therefore, so that no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if black comes out only because of the medicine that has been put on, which has power, then you should squeeze a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one drachm of resin, and mix it with oil; and put it on the medicine
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the cure with the manner of cures that he knows, until it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that neither time are broken the two parts of the neck above, or one by itself, because they are bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and this shoulder is cartilaginous and does not break unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you plug your little finger or the tip of the neck, and make it even within your index finger, and at the back by defect, until the neck revives according to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain because of your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if his break is in the upper part of the neck and cannot return to its place, know that you put it equal to the head of a stick a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the broken part is of two sides, do it otherwise, and make haste to restore the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or ninth, when the abscesses have subsided, then bind the head with linen bandages, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you bind one to another, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and may the bandages be so thick that they fill the apertures of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that one must dampen the strips to make them soft, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It seems to me that this is not good, but it will be if they are wet with the ash of oak and the powder of mulberry.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then remove the bandages when the bone is hard and the joints toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never bind the neck with goose feathers in place of bandages, and if a wound needs wrapping several times, and the fracture is mended, and blow on the patient.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or make the knot well so that you can see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess forms while you are operating, put cotton soaked in oil or a poultice of blood-root, or a small patch of dyak.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscesses don't come out, then wet plaster with flour from wheat and incense powder, mixed with sheep's dung, and put on light coats, and tie no loops.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the bones is small, and they are broken into small pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments for this, then cut off the piece, and treat the injured parts with suitable plasters and oils.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no pain inside the bones, then treat the outside, and put on plaster until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	From the rupture of the jaw.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not too large, and it is not broken into two pieces, but rather bent inside, then one must take care lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, when the fracture is on the right side, that you pierce your little finger with a needle on the patient's left side.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is on the left mandible, then pierce your little finger on the right side with a needle, and pierce the fracture lightly, and do it with the other hand on the opposite side, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is in two parts, then you should bring them together with two extensions, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the deeps comes, or a rupture, if it is drawn from a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw with cerot, and put on a double drape.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on the drape a great well-made stele, or a piece of leather even, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the musket you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure has changed, if you release it on the third day, and then reset to its place what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put plaster on it, of the powder from the mill with much ash or flour of straw, after that you have removed the cerot;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on the other plaster a light thing, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as long as he is healthy;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times are saned in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if you see that the figure [of the wound] changes, if you desalinate at the third day, and then put back to place what has changed; and apply plaster, of the powder of the mill with much salt or flour of sisament, after you have taken out the cerote; and put on the other light plaster, and if the plaster applies itself, and the disposition of the ill one does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times is healthy in III weeks.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and a wound together, do not repair it with a bone piece;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtile of the oster as instruments convenient to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, expand it with fire according to necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all the pieces of bone together, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, put on it plasters suitable for this, to prevent infection, until it is healed.
de la forcele	(Here comes the end)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The force him to break many times before, around the shoulder, and the break is so according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where it is broken and torn in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the overtures are so when the break is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one twists the shoulder that does not break with force;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck toward the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then set equal the break on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or twist.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you are skilled at making it larger, then put a round staff of linen or cloth on the shoulder of the patient, and make it as big as you need.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and keep the force on, and hold the staff at your side, so that you make the break even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the spear out to the end, so that it comes completely off, it is appropriate for the patient to lie down on his back, and put the shoulder with the help of a minister, and hold the shoulder away, until the bone of the spear is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then place the break at your sides, and if you find any debris, then cut on top of it;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and work the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then take a patch to one of the incisions you have made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put aside this forcep instrument, for surgery.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it should be like a spoon, and not too narrow, and as wide as is necessary according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and there are two heads, so that you see them, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, just like the split in the wound you made when you broke the bone.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you have heated the abscess to the point where it splits open, and the split is small, or if you doubt about heating the abscess, then wrap it in a cloth or tent according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, if you moisten it with oil, honey, and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The extraction of the bone, when there are wounds and no bruising, is that you put on the bone the powder from the millstone and saffron, and apply light staples, and insert a spike where you need it;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very long bandage about a palm wide, then put two cloth strips over the staples, and cover with powder.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin stick about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the top of the bandage is hidden.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the stick on the breach, and return the bandage to the neck, and loosen the healthy shoulder, and tighten the sick shoulder.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and take away from each part, and when you see that the time is right for the stick to hold the breach properly, and see clearly that the stick does not move over the broken bone, let it remain each day, and when the bandage loosens, if it needs to be tightened;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and have the sick one lie on his back, and put him down when he sleeps in a small position, to raise the shoulder;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if the breach becomes stiffer by the alignment of the shoulder, or if you put the arm around the neck, and do not take it off unless there is a sudden accident, until 20 days have passed;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then begin to apply the plaster again if you see that it is necessary, and tighten and leave it like this until it has healed;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and she was restored in 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Now it comes that the shoulder is broken or out of place, and does not move only by touch;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the apparatus is arranged according to the figure of the fracture, and you reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the powder of the mill with plenty of flour, and light touches, and put on a double sheet;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on a wide and thin steel, a little wider than the shoulder, and despatch the steel at all places of the shoulder, so to employ the linen stitches, so that the steel is even;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it with a strong bandage all around, so that the steel does not move from its place, and inspects it every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and whenever he becomes loose again, if it is held in place, and makes the bone equal if it has moved from its place, and lies the patient on his back;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is reset after XX days or XXV days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when the number of days is completed, if it becomes loose again, and be careful, for it is not bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If there is a piece of the bone forward, and don't remove it, if it heats, and the bone, and do as we said in the dislocation of the shoulder to soothe abscess heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The arms are never broken in midair, but this happens sometimes.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But they are often broken at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when they are broken in the middle, if they decline to the side, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a lack of support, and at times, and by chance he vomits blood, and opens the veins in the broken bone, and it smells bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the reset should be such that the patient lies down on his back, and puts I cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and gathers the ribs with your hands, and carefully makes it equal in all ways as much as you can, until the bone figure is like it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	and put on plasters and stoppings thereon the thin stone of salt, or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and return the thread roundly to the back, and fastens it tightly, and loosens it hour by hour, and if it relaxes, so that it is held fast;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to loosen it, because of rust or because of itching that comes to the joint, or pain or abscess, if you hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster, and treat him in a way that suits his cure;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove the plaster, and hold it tight until he is well.
de la brisure des costes	of the rupture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the broken ribs come from the back only a little way down, and at the top towards the inside, and do not bend much because they are thin;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the smell is good to the inquiry as are due.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And restore them so that you make the rupture even, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on plaster, and a splint from a stick if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	If the ribs break and fall inward, the patient feels great pain and a sharp pain as if he were crying, because the bone rubs against the membrane.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and it is sore pinched and twisted, and it has great pains in the back, and this causes great harm to health, and the old have great trouble.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of these serve that it is necessary to administer meat that swells the belly, in order to push the rupture away.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We must not do this, for if hot poultices are not brought, they will not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, and the wound is healed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And no one of us says that we put suction cups on top, to suck out liquid, and this seems reasonable to me.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, I have the doubt that the suction cup does not attract the excesses to the place for the arrangement of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should not cover the spot with another moist thing in oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the wound even, then it is cured with the cure for ulcers, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because the bone rubs against the membrane, there is doubt about the patient, then it is good to split along the line of the ribs that are broken, and it is good to put a tool to prevent the wound from healing.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one should cut the bone, and draw it gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it is well.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses develop, then put them on cloths soaked in oil, and put them on the wound;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal while waiting for the head of the abscess to come out, and wash it well on the coast where it is, until it is well.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the throat
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No times does a breaker come to break the neck bone, and poke so that he bleeds;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this has happened to anyone, and you do not know if he will be well or not, then take care that his hands are soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or stretch them out; and when you prick them with a pin, if he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many cases, and if he does not feel them when they are pricked and does not move them, know that the joint of the bone has been saved, and the disease has been cured, if one puts on a cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you do not know whether it is well or not, if one's bones are softened, and one's accident is in one's hands, and on one's back windiness and excretion without will;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one makes her lie on her back, there is involuntary expulsion.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it has been treated by being placed on its back and it cannot move, then it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If he does not work hard at his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident did not come to him, then this is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is such that if there is an abscess, you rub it with oil or sheep's fat, until it is calm;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then put on one of the plasters, drying it and binding it, and command the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is well.\
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes loose, then cover it with oil;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and set the bone, then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a sutură, until it is well;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone of the skull is broken, which is called "the skull-key", then you hold your pouch in your left hand and place it evenly with your right hand, then apply the plaster and tie it up, if you need to do so;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then tighten it, and if there is a dislocated bone, then mend it, and the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	For the fracture of the leg bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	But if the bone of the thigh is broken, and if there were to be, then there would only be a little damage to the skull.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And put it long and flat in the bed, so that the pain and swelling come to the patient, and not elsewhere, and break what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration should be that you hold your hand over it, as long as you are above the broken part;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and knows what is the break and form of him;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the break is at the top, so make it equal to that break, as long as it is in natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines inward, then make the patient stand on his stomach as long as the rehabilitation of that fracture is arranged for him.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it equal, then place it on the plaster, and then place a beam of wood or a post on top of it, and stretch the break, so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and employ the use of splints on the sides, as long as the length is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if the abscess comes up, do not scratch it, as long as the abscess is calm, and then place on it what we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and hold it as is right, if there is no bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	This is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The auxillary joint is that which is between the collar and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of the two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	If one is that you take a strong pulse, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And let the two shoulders be tied together and raised up, and cut the patient on one side;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then let them put some arms above the patient, so that it comes to rest, and have a cart of wood then put on top of any heavy thing or the ministers extend downward;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then let the surgeon cut it evenly with his hands together, as long as the knife returns in the right way.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that one should let the patient rest on his back, and tie his hands to his neck, then order two ministers that one of them tie who is lying on the side with his hands, and the others pull him by all his body, and extend each to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too much, then tie the patient by all his body, and extend each minister to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the surgeon is near the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary that you put the strong pulse behind the shoulder, and the other towards the neck, away from the knife.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And if the surgeon is near the neck, then it is necessary to put the light pulse lightly, without effort, as long as the knife is even on both sides, and on the neck;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	and then make the break even, as it should be, and hold fast, if an abscess comes up.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess comes up, if one does not hold it back for seven days, and puts on a damp cloth and rose oil, until the abscess is relieved;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then hold it back, and the way to hold it back is that you put the plaster on the break, then join the arm to the aid, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the cloth on, and hold back on the aid, and on the arm so that the arm is in a good position, if nothing is causing it to move, or if the bone has not been broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use aids, and put on the break a bigger and stronger aid than the others, and have between each aid two spaces, and let each aid be so big that it goes over the break by three inches on each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then drag on the stakes, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the paste on the breach, stronger and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the stakes and the dragging, as we have said, in the ooze that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, let it be tied up for seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then watch for three days to see if the itch does not flare up again and does not come back to the member, or the painful sensation does not come back because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you dub the apotheosis, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if such an accident does not come, do not untie it before three or more days, and let the patient sleep on his back and keep his hands on his stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put a layer of clean, even wool on the shoulder, and watch every hour of the day or night to see if the shape of the broken member does not change, or if the bonds are not loosened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If it is to be given by virtue of medicine, and give the meat that we have put before in such a way that the meat is at the first subtle.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to take effect, if it is thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be recovered in 40 days from all;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then you must remove and administer bath and medicines of ointments to the shoulder to heal it.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stiffness is bad and blocked, it should not be separated after one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of II bones, which are called "fosciles", one of which is small, and it is this which gives the hand its shape;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is this which is dislocated, towards the small one;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	maybe breaking only the big "foscile", or maybe both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small "foscile" is broken, the restoration is easy and the recovery is rapid;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large ones are broken, if the healing is ill, and more painful than when they are broken all together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If this small piece of wood has been broken by a slight blow, then it is necessary to extend it slightly and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if the large one is deformed, then it must be extracted with greater force;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on one cussin, and make the pouchet of the hand higher than the other two, and the smaller ones lower than the others, and let the patient lie across it, and the cussin in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no effort;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the ministers of his arms to the part that is wounded to his hand, or to the chains, and other ministers to the other above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then make it even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If the wood has broken into pieces, then place each piece in its proper place; and if one of them has become loose and does not fit, and you cannot restore it to its place, then fix it with iron and bone, as we have said above.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the breaking there is a wound, then I have spoken of this to the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration abscesses form, then bind them with a cloth made of rosin oil and white wax, so that they are neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and dip it gently from above, until the abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	and then coat the bone, and I put the ointment of the powder from the mill with a lot of wax, then put the splints on, and let the splint of the break be a little tighter, and a little wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it should have six splints or more in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	either that the break is in one bone, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold it up higher than the other part, and always further away, as I said at the beginning about the ointment;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the liniments that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, which is being held up, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And wait for the member and the lien after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itch that comes to the member, it is right that you wet the member with hot water, until the itch is calm.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member not be too tight to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again to draw out, and if the lien is softened and the bone exposed, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it is necessary that the member not be moved again for a long time, because it is too stiff, then you must soften it slightly and leave it thus for some days, so that the movement begins again, and then draw it out.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, let it not be dislocated until XX days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or, with the head turned, then bind his hands to his neck, and let his necks be even, and guard against movement and turning over, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this breaker is healed in 30 days or in 35, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexes of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	are few fractures on the back of the hand, and there comes but little rain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is right that the patient cut it, and make it even straight in front of him;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the extended loom, and extend the broken bones, and make them even mirror-like, until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and with the plaster and the staples, if abscesses do not come then I put a stake according to the quantity of the place;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in I wrap it in linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the spear is at the back between the navel of the plant, then I make a stake of drapels, and instruct the patient to strangle it to his bruised plant;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then the stake of a long drapel, and be the stake of curd also as great as the plant of the hand, and strangles it, so that it comes.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks on the outside, then it is fitting that you put a stake above, and another one in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it completely around the hand, and stop the blood flow between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the spear comes to any of us two, if it is poked, then he sets it even, so that it comes;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and strangles it with the plant, and you see if I put a straight small stake to lift the bruised one, and does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if it is broken in two, as in the index or one of the others, if it is made equal, and laid with its healthy partner which follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all together, that they may move freely, or you set one on a stake, as if it were a pestle;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and arrangement of an abscess, and protect him who comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken chest
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The flesh of the loins is often broken, and one can see well when it returns before and after.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration should be such that you tie them together above the break, and below too.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his link equally to his sides;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and that is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the breast, then one of the bonds extends beyond the knuckle, and the other bond below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And so if it's close to the knee, then let the leg be removed from the knee, and let the knee be bent down.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then take the bone with its two hands so that it is according to its natural shape, and then put on the plaster and the bandage, so that it does not move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is an abscess, if he leaves it calm then return to your work and your treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The rest is done in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap it in a strong cloth or a wooden board twice or three times, and hold back the excess, then bring the leg so that the heels come to the root of the ankle, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, away from the knee joint, and bring the end of the thread up;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn to the leg and to the thigh the bandage, then put on the splint bones, and put a splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then employ the fire cautery between the leg and the thigh of linen bandages in order to make even the stretching, then begin to bind in a three- or fourfold knot on the splint;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go up on the splint, and less the stretching;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then enter the two wires that you have threaded between the leg and the thigh, and in their place three splints, then return to the distention at the head of the wire, as long as you can remove the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it steady so that it does not move from its place, then let it be like that, and if it does not come back with an abscess or swelling or any other sign.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, if it slips, and turns this way or that, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are any pieces of bone that grip, if necessary, let them be.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if it cannot, if necessary, split the joint, and draw forcefully;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy again.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never break the chest in this case, if one sets a splint, as with the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, when restoring it in this way, do not let the patient move.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the collarbone is restored in a day or two or more, depending on the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	There is little breaking in the knee, but it swells many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, let there be only a split or a crack, and not all at once, and not too deep; and if it does not hurt, then let it be fixed in this way, so that it no longer hurts.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is done by setting equal what is long on one side and short on the other, until it is joined together, if possible, without moving;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then set the plaster, and put a round splint on it, if you need one, and hold it as necessary, then restore all the provisions that we have said for other breaks, such as hot and cold applications, and similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If each person has an accident like this, then he must remain healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	regarding the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	I understand that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken like this in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is like that of the arm which is even, and the work is all done; And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns all around.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, then turn back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, then great pain is felt, and it can be seen clearly.
et torne desoz.	Then it straightens out.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then extend it, and make it even, and bind the joints evenly;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	However, if the breaking is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension must be smaller and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and adjust accordingly to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	and when you have finished your work, if the person has hair that touches the leg on both sides and is long from the ankle to the knee,
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap two bends around the leg above and below, and place it in the middle, and at this length do not let the leg fall to the right or to the left, and so is good;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should administer any oil along the length of the leg, and if necessary, and put the leg in such a way that it does not move, and properly do this to the fracture or wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each leg every day, to see if there is an abscess or another accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the treatment until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but at the foot there is a break in two cases and only one time; it has happened to me in more than one condition.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a fracture of the foot and you see the bones coming together, put the sick person on the ground as if they wanted to walk, and then now put your foot on their own, where the bones are raised, and press them until they go back into their place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And then put the plaster and press it on, and place a small table at the feet with II flat shoulders, and then fasten it to the ground in front of you, and then you have wrapped the drapes around, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four are passed, then unclasp him, because you will find the bones even if they are broken or out of place.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are any two broken, restore them, and as we have said to the two by hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then put on the two broken a plate according to the length of the two, and let it be a little wider, then place at the feet the small table that I said, and fasten it to the ground in front of you;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three more broken, put on each a plate according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen drape, and fasten the small table at the feet;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be placed on top of the small table with the stomach of the foot so that it is well covered.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other breakers, when we have said it.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and heal each injury so as it should be healed.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone with a blunt knuckle
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the woman's bones are broken, if she is seated enlarged, then she leans to the back part, and is held by behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the hole of nature with cotton disease, and put also big as I sit;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then stand the woman up, and slowly bend her back and again jump the cotton, until it comes to the entry of nature, and the bones come back with slow sitting;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, if she jumps the cotton, and when she has urinated, it is put back, and thus do seven days or more;
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	so will be restored the break, and if you see, take a bladder of biber, and tie a cord to the navel, and pour all the bladder into nature;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow up the bladder until it is inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the break will heal itself;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton and leave it for a few days until he is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bones of the hand or foot of the man or woman are broken, if he sets it as we have said regarding the hip bone.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these wounds are not hidden from him who puts his mind to it and takes care of it, and listen to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the break signifies more than a few things in the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	let them eat then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the groin, when it is broken, take a neck of goose and pour the urine into the groin;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it in linen bandages, and leave it for three days or so, and he will be well without surgery.
de brisure avec plaie	with break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is appropriate for the one who has broken with a wound, even if it is great, as with the hip bone or shoulder blade or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healers that we have described testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals well, if the vitriol scar remains, then you should continue to restore the rupture in that very same hour, or else the blisters will come on that day.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the blisters come on, and you postpone the restoration until the next day, as long as the blisters are calm, and do not touch them either on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is protruding through the skin, it is necessary that you bring the bone to a standstill lightly with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extensions have not appeared to you so that your hands are made equal, if it is with this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight inches long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this it is necessary that he should put III or IVI, according to what is necessary in each treatment of fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member when opening it, and be sharp at the end, and thick in the middle ahead: thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	is called "planche", because it is necessary that the bent head be placed on the top of the prominent bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and be straightened once, as often as possible, and be equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the tool cannot take the bone well, it is necessary that you cope with the head of the bone as long as the instrument has the ability to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, with an appropriate instrument, either an incision or a saw, to your power;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And look at this man who is delayed in the bone of the neck and small fractures.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If he remains in his place, then wet the cloth with wine-colored tar, and thoroughly smear it on him;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put tar or anything else on the wound where there is oil, that he does not cause sores and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	And then apply poultices when you have reduced the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering around it well, according to the quantity of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not drawn up with the fracture;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times have they done this foolish thing, and have brought upon the patient death or corrupting nothing;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And may be the dislocations are softer and more delicate than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, then it does not fit to put a splint on.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap in linen, instead of splints, hard drapes, and bind it fast.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days to have been infected the wound, if he is there that you put on top of all water, and I put poultices healing wounds, so as poultice tetrafarmacion and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs are moved so that the wound runs down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes, and it cannot be joined but runs together again, knowing that there are small pieces of bone; because it is necessary that you wash the wound with water, and all these troublesome pieces that bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to light, or any other kind of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and opened upon the limb, as the neck-bone or the shoulder-bone, and other great limbs, do not pull it out, for often death comes from this, but let it putrefy.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	in case it should break again after 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound, if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	the bruses that come from the sudore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come after the health of the broken one, even when it is near a joint, and an ugly sight is the figure of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and for a chance cannot do their natural work of the limbs.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then, so that we are not fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if the ministering of medicines is in a sticky state, as in aloe, incense, myrrh, and sarcocollus, acacia, and other things like that, so that you do not press any of these things, or all together, and confound them with wine stuck with resin or with a lot of ash or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on the neck in layers, and bind them well, and do not release them by hand every day;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislocates it, and begins another one, until the nodulations are broken;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you strain on a well-made piece of cloth;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of the cloth is that it breaks all the nodules off the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if his swelling is hardened as stone, he is fit for the oven, so that when cooked, it shows the excess flesh clearly.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Or you take him to no razor, as long as he is oiled, and cure him as long as he is well.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member which is weak after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the break in the bone has healed, and the limbs remain weak and fragile, this may happen for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	for one is because it was tied too tight, and was not tied as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or for one there are too many ligaments, and cannot bring the member into its natural position;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or for many armpits;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or for great movements, not in his hour;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or for one has little blood in his body, and are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is such that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the sin is multiplied in him.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and the minister give bath, and do joy and let sleep;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put wax on the member, so that the wax attracts his great swelling, and dip it often in hot water, until the swelling runs to the member;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two injured limbs after surgery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural work:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	so do not believe the foolish who serve this one must break the member all over again, and many foolish people have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these works are to blame, and they bring great evils, and perhaps death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	all ways, let the nodules and the torture be fresh, so that they are raised from hot water, or that herbs are cooked that soften them, as foil of swan, and roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and the fabric made soft with a softening agent, as well done squirt, and you take the muskeg of swan, and confit it with fat or oil of lamb's ear, and make an ointment;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take figs, and grind them with hay of coles, and similar medicines that soften the sudden pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the osteum rubbed constantly and lengthily with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	So that each limb is moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the torture is old and hard, as stone, and it needs to be split with iron, then cover it up to the bone, with a sharp knife, lightly;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put on the poultice and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now brought back gently.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if delayed, if the veins swell, and perhaps if he is reset to his place at the site of injury.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	For by chance do not move him when he is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times cause pain and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	however, when this happens, if the patient is made well, then leave him, until the abscess has been calmed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and heal each member as the wound heals in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the potions for the dislocations of the shoulders just up to the height of the piez.
des mandibules	of the mandible
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It should be known that the mandibles are dislocated from both sides, and the dislocation of both is according to two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	either they are a little out of place, and slightly soft. Or
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	either they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the floor, and the saliva of his mouth so that he cannot hold it back, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return by means of these four dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then you must bring it to the hospital quickly and do not delay.
