et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	And in this way that the ministers tie the head of the sick person, and pour mirres some pottage of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, there are two parts of dislocation;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands be away, to put even;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And command to the sick person that he softens his jaws and moves them from all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the wound heal evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is brought back, most especially if they are both jaws together, then raise them with warm water and oil, until they are reset lightly;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not delay in bringing it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset even and the mouth of the sick person is closed well with a softener, then put upon it drapings wet with an oil made of rosin and wax, and let it rest lightly;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient lie on his back, and his shoulders be between two pillows, so that he does not move to the left or right, or try to turn over, but eat light food until the pains are gone and the jaw has recovered.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then after he has eaten lightly, and does not work to open his mouth for eating or drinking until the jaw is well healed and recovered.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and do not return to their places, then fever and abnormal sweating will come, and by chance there will be a solution of the stomach, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, know that it is a sign of improvement;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and often dies those to whom it is given, in nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not release from the coast within the extension of the thread inside it, and is dislocated only once at the back, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the recovery is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the dislocated joint with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put the splint and bandage on and hold it in place;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head that is over the neck cannot be dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it is not moved again, and if it is never dislocated, so he returns to his place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put a splint and bandage on it, and hold it in place, and instruct the patient to rest as long as he is well;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in the same way you should reset the shoulder when it is out of place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder can only be dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	that one is when it is dislocated at the part of the shoulder joint;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the breastbone;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance it is dislocated at the top part, and this happens sometimes;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and never dislocate behind for the shoulder, and never dislocate inside for the neck;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times dislocates toward the shoulder, more so at those who have little hair, for to them this salt shall be taken away without surgery.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	For those who have enough hair, they will get better without surgery, and return to being healthy.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that they beat or break, and the shoulder is heated by a hot abscess, and they think that it has been dislocated.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	So then you must test it out, as long as you are certain of it.
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And this is how dislocations happen when they go down toward the shoulder, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find various manifest differences.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and at the head of the shoulder there is a pit, and dislocate the shoulder on the table where the head of the shoulder is, just like it were an egg.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor move at all;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and if it is dislocated from above, then is it not hidden, for you see it clearly in the towel.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this method of dislocation is not to be used when it is new, or when the patient is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the way is that the minister should lift the hand of the sick person upward, then put the splint on the joint, and raise it up by force.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the minister should lift the hand, and extend it upward, then put it on.
si venra hastanment.	then come to the hospital.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if not as we have said above with hand movements, then it is convenient for the sick person to be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and provide a softening and soothing treatment, as an infusion of althaea and fenugreek and melilote in water, and be administered.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then let the patient lie on their back, and place the shoulder's axil on a stool of another equal, not too soft nor too hard, then put the mirrour of the foot on the stool, and gently lift up the shoulder with care, and pull the hand of the sick.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and others ministers dryve the head of the sick man, so that he does not move down;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder comes back right away, and you will see if it comes back in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you make be present a man who is greater than the sick one;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be two sides of the chest, and set the axil of the sick man, and lift up the axil upwards so that the sick man hangs by his arms;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and others ministers pull the hand of the sick man down towards his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then with him put something heavy, so that the dislocation comes back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And they also answer in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is placed a long rod in the ground, so that the shoulder is also caused as if by a pistol, and it is not too large nor too small;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then let the patient be placed, but that there are drapels of sweat on it, and the patient is standing on the long wood;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then his hand is extended from one side to the other, forming a loop, and the joint will return to its place peacefully;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, then this remedy is done:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a long wood of two arms of great length and four fingers wide, which has the head placed so that it can enter perfectly into the shoulder joint, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then place it on the wood with the drapels of sweat, so that the wood does not hurt the patient, and then put it into the shoulder joint of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend your arms above the wood of a long stick, and place the shoulder on the wood, and the arm at the top of the hand, then put the arm on an escutcheon of a shield of width, and let the hands be extended downward, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint is now ready.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	Then when it is in place, in whatever way it may be, you must put an even woolen needle, then set the plaster ready with powder from the mill, with incense and amber, on the whole shoulder and innards, then draw it away forward, and tie it to the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let your hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he suck a little, so that the members are comfortable, because he will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then suck a little more after 5 or 7 days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is stiff and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of its place due to moisture that has come or due to some other cause, you must apply cauterization three times, as it is done with the paste of cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it relaxes after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise your arms upstream, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or extended or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joints never fit back in their place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	When dislocation is due to a fall or push, and stretching of the hands, and another place is administered;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes to the limb greasiness, and slowly moving, then the patient often bathes, until that greasiness is gone, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the head
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joints of the neck are dislocated and return to their place.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation cannot be restored, for we can see it and feel it clearly;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with good health, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is deformed, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it in such a way that the bones come together as they should, for if the bones do not come together, there would be great pain in resetting them.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and may not be reset from all sides, especially at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	Si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li Mors.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	This is worse than other dislocations, and it causes greater pain, and sometimes death. And if it can be done, so that it can be brought back, you should hold its hand with both of yours;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and its arms spread out, and the hands with their thumbs in line with the neck at the back and at the front, and push the joint into place together with the palm roots, until it recovers its position;
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocations are in front, so that when it doubles its hand to its other hand, and raises its wrist, it returns to its place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	If it does not return to its position, give it a strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and two minister extend the arm, and two turn it, so that it does not move at the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	Then turn the arm of each side, then you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when he touches the joint to his hand, if it does not come from any oil to soften the joint, then draw the joint together so that it regains its shape.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, if put on plaster dry with ash of owl, and strain it together, and bend the arm at the shoulder of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then loose it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, if loosen the ligature, and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not fit well, if start again the plaster and the ligature, and leave it for a few days, until it is firmly in place;
puis le deslie.	then loose it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, if bathe and rub it well, and press until it is eased;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	put on top of the joint a piece of thick lamb skin, then leave it for a day and a night, then the bone, and make it enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the skin back on, and then bring it into the bath again;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then do this two or three times until it is healthy;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see pus, put on top of the wound a warm, butter-soaked cloth, and squeeze it out;
si revenra a sa disposition.	then return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The dislocated joint of the hand returns more easily than the joints of the other members do.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to put it back in place as soon as possible while it is still dislocated, so that the bones do not swell or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And let them stretch out the hand of the disease on a table, and extend the fingers, and make it even, so that it put its palm on the appearance of the joint, and hold it until it recovers.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Anyway, you must look to see if it is in the right place.
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the diseased back of the hand on a table for extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then put the patient's hand flat on the table and bring it to rest: then look to see if it is well in place;
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the extraction of painful abscesses causes them to break open, and he leaves it like that without recapping.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after a few days, then the joint will be twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not ask the patient to do anything but let his hands remain moist until they can extract anything completely.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Then you know that the nerve is cut, or an artery.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other remedy than to extract by cautery the case, and perhaps nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have said, then extract it and leave it for V days, then take it off and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no crack, if the wet warm water, and rub until he is cured.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two bones of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never are dislocated the joints of the hand to each side, never at the back of the palm or the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then hold the two together and draw them back into place as much as possible, then support the head of the bone with your hand, and move it towards the joint where it is dislocated;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it there for a day, then make it even again that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and do not move it if you have done so, and dislodge it from day to day, and make it move, and then relace it in place;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do so often, until it is loose, and in the same way if it is dislocated at the base of the hand, and do so as you have done above, until it is well;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and also do this, when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the spine of the neck
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there will be no cure, for it quickly kills the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the excretions come forth without will, cannot be held, and often soften any member, or both legs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the spine moves to four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which mutates in the rear is called "gilbositez".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the cure is that you treat it if the gilibosite has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no cure or recovery from all of it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of curing with great words do not bring any great benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have simplified it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gilibosite that comes from the back before the chest, there is neither beginning nor cure;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and I say that what comes straight in two sides, and cannot be cured except properly what comes at the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	is that the patient is lying down with his face flat and has no pressure on him so he does not get hurt;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then put a piece of wood under his head forming an arch, and another one at the feet, and tie with a cord the legs of the patient behind him, and another one at the ankles, and at the knees;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and the two ministers know the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two beams;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they are well closed, the beam as we have said, and the mirrour sets its palms on the spine forming, until it comes back;
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not come back by this cure, then take a round table of three arms long, and tilt it away from the wall, and let the patient be on one side, and pour the water of the table away from the wall, and then put the middle of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and place its legs on top of the other head of the table, and press firmly, until it regains its position.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you see, do so with the palm that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And that you place two torches at the head of the patient with one arm, and between them, and a palm's width apart, longwise;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each torch a hole, or the torche runneth, and let the torches be firmly set in the ground, so that they do not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each pair of torches have a single torch, so that the line turns, and have two small torches, a palm's width longwise, to turn the line;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then lie the line that is among the torches towards the palm of the hand at the head, and the other line towards the legs at the other torch, and each servant turns its torch along the whole line, and the master sets the line evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then put on desiccating plaster with much chalk, and then the poultices, and then the tablet of III feet long, which, as we have said, must be red to the place of gloom and the part of the spine sound, and bind with a thread, so that the patient uses subtle fasting until he is well;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if there is no improvement at the end of this time, then administer softening and soothing medicines with the tablet we have described above;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and never give a piece of lead, and never does the appearance come in the lower spine at the back, and be careful that it is dislocations;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	is the bone that opens, for one must not have any presumptions:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	may bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Here is the translation of the text:
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Saiches that as the joints of the hip and as the joints of the shoulder come only from dislocations alone, not coming at all as with the other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parties:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	behind and in front;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and behind them there is a little more, and in front and behind them.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of his dislocations inside is that when one joins the leg with the sick, it is longer and more open than the healthy, and the patient's knees cannot double their knees at all.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the time which is necessary for the wound to heal after an abscess has been cut, so that the head of the thigh comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes at death, if this accident is opposite to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of who has it in front, are that he has his leg well according to the fulfillment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	all ways, do not double the knee joint pain, and if you make it run, it can not before, and holds back his urine, and swell the ankle, and when he goes, so he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it comes behind, if he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in its place between the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The patients who have this kind of dislocation should be cared for if the dislocation is old and it takes time to heal according to its condition, otherwise there is no cure;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it is not necessary that he has presumptuousness.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in those who have a fresh dislocation, and there are four ways of dislocation, you must hurry to restore the joint, and put it back in place and move it to the right and left, and twist it from side to side;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	So that it does not come back, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not come back in this way, you must have a strong assistant, and hold the leg very firmly with two hands, or tie it to the knee with a piece of cloth;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and others extend their hand above in such a way that they pour water on their palms, and then tie it with a string from the knuckle;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and others tie the head of the limb;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend forwards and backwards all at once, so that the patient is raised from the ground all at once, and remains stationary.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then one should treat its appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocations are in the parry, then one should raise the patient on his side, then tie the string to the root of the elbow, and the limb that is out of place, then extend the string upwards towards the elbow, and downwards towards the forceps;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	and others extend their arms, and embrace the large ring of the elbow that is ill, and extend it away from the body form;
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	If they return to their place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot fix it in this way as we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong rope from the sole of one foot to the sole of the other, and from the thigh of the leg that is extended to that of the other, and keep the patient's legs extended more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then hang them by the neck from a beam, and have one arm outstretched on the ground;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	and command one minister to embrace the head of the shoulder, and have other ministers hanging with the patient who embraces the shoulder so that the dislocation returns to its place quite quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation has gone out, so lie the patient down, as we have said in the case of one with gibbus, and remove the rope from the leg that is wrong properly, and also from the stone;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then take two tongs, one at the head and another at the base, then insert a tong between the toes at the patient's foot and pull it towards the shape;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and place wet towels inside, so that it does not hurt the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and have him put his hand in a position to reset the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on a table, and press him as we have said in gibbosity, and make the patient lie on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocations are forward, so it is necessary to extend the injured leg far away, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place him on his back on the injured side, then press with the other hand, and extend it towards the groin;
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocations are on the side, it is not necessary to extend the injured person below, nor to raise them onto the ground, rather they should be laid out on their sides as we have said for sleeping on the two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let it lie on its face, and extend the leg as we have said before, and you must all press upon the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and will be fixed when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then set the bones, and put on the plaster, and extract it from a bandage so that the shin does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three or four days, then remove it, and put on the plaster;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, extract it as before, and leave it for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then remove it, and let him go blithely, until the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The dislocated limb is to be reset according to three methods:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inside and outside, and behind;
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not delay.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	and do not lag behind. If the leg does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the rehabilitation of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and place his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee with your palms, and pull apart your toes, then bend the two sides of the knee in turn;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and other ministers extend his foot until the genitals return to their place, and the sign is that he bends his leg at the knee easily;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on, and make the leg bend at the knee, and keep them together firmly for three or four days, then release it;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not work on the sick to move until the members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, then give a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation at the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never dislocated and never fully displaced, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and test before the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	They should be brought if they are light, and must be extended lightly to their hands when they are first touched.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated from the top, you must make the patient sit up straight and support him with his ministers away from the leg, above the ankle joint;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then teach the foot to you at your right hand, and then at your left twice, and then extend it upwards, and blow strongly on the foot upwards;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, blowing and teaching the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, it is good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, if the effort begins again, because it returns;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return like this, then make the sick person sit on his back on the ground, and put something firmly in the ground between his buttocks, and tie the sheets around it so that it does not hurt the sick person.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then place the minister's thigh, and another minister extends the leg to its hands or ties it, so that he lies on the collar of the stone;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each minister evenly, and the rope is close between the sick person's buttocks to hold the sick person in place when they are extended;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then place the minister' even on the dislocation at his hands, and another minister ties the healthy leg to the side, and the dislocation will come back slowly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is done, then put the plaster on and press it down, and strain it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the ties are not too tight;
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	and leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if he holds on to it, let him stretch it.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then let it rest for three days or four, and don't go out for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that term is up, it is not yet certain that he will still be dislocated.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come to the foot, so that you calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, until they are well.
des dois	the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, so it is best to gently extend them without work, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any of the joints of the back or foot, then you must make the patient sit with his back or leg straight up on a bed or bench, and put your foot on what opens up those joints, and press down on your foot gently, until he regains feeling;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even, and he does not move anything, then set the heel of his foot on a table at two joints, then stretch it gently, and leave it for three days, then let him rest;
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him rest, until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When the wound comes with a dislocation and it is restored, many times the patient has died:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow to anger, do not be bold:
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning of things calming aposteme with hot, and leave the patient in God's hands, unless you see hope of health:
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, if you set the member back in place now, so that the hot apses come;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is in place, if you administer calming apses, and cure the wound, as it should be, with drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and with dislocation there is fracture, and small bones are dislocated, if the bone, and do what we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and keep away from a place of fear, according to what I have said, because it will cost you your soul according to your creator, and for the sake of arming yourself and your body.
